The Single Term and Eternal Knowledge
The author states the Sunni doctrine on the single term and its basis in eternal knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine that every person has a single appointed term determined by Allah's eternal knowledge, and that even the slain person dies by that term.

Core Idea
Every death is by a single term decreed eternally by Allah.

This lesson presents the foundational Sunni doctrine on predestination regarding life and death. The author begins by affirming that each person has one fixed term, and no action can alter it. This is grounded in Allah's eternal knowledge, as indicated by the Quranic verse about the Preserved Tablet. Understanding this key principle will help you see why Mu'tazilite alternatives are rejected.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, focusing on the author's opening assertion and the Quranic citation. Let the words settle before moving to the translation.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two key claims
Notice that the author makes two connected claims: (1) the term is one, (2) the slain person dies by that term. Then he links this to Allah's eternal knowledge and quotes the Quran.
3
Understand the Quranic proof
The verse (13:39) refers to Allah's erasing and confirming decrees, with the Preserved Tablet as the source. The author uses it to show that only what Allah eternally knows actually occurs.
4
Reflect on the phrase 'this is the position of Ahl al-Haqq'
This statement distinguishes the Sunni position from others. Recognize that the lesson is not just informative but also doctrinal—it marks orthodoxy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيانُ أنَّ الأجل واحد والمقتولُ مَيِّتُ بأجله، ثم يؤول إلى موجب علمه سبحانه على ما يشير إليه قوله تعالى: يَمْحُوا اللَّهُ مَا يَشَاءُ وَيُثْبِتُ وَعِندَهُ أُمُّ الْكِتَبِ، فالمعتبر إنما هو ما تعلَّق العلمُ الأزليُّ ببلوغه، هذا ما عليه أهل الحق. وغير هذا من مذاهب المخالفين، كمذهب الكعبي من المعتزلة: أنَّ المقتول ليس بميت؛ لأنَّ القتل فعل العبد، والموت فعله تعالى وأثر صنعه، فالمقتول له أجلان القتل والموت وأنَّه لو لم يُقتل لعاش إلى أجله الذي هو الموت. وكمذهب الكثير من المعتزلة أنَّ القاتل قطع على المقتول أجله، وأنَّه لو لم يُقتل لعاش إلى أمد هو أجلُه الذي علم الله موته فيه لولا القتل، أو لمات في ذلك الوقت باطل أي غير مطابق للواقع؛ لمنافاته القواطع التي لا تقبل التأويل، وكل باطل لا يقبل عند العقلاء المتمسكين بالحق. وخمسون مثلا، وهو في علم الله تعالى مُقيّد بأن لا يفعل طالعة مثلا؛ وإن فعلها فله ستون. وسبق في علمه أنه يفعلها، فالزيادة على ما في الصحف، فهي زيادة بحسب الظاهر.
An explanation that the term is one and the slain person dies by his term, then it refers to the requirement of His knowledge, may He be exalted, as indicated by His saying: Allah eliminates what He wills and establishes, and with Him is the Mother of the Book. So the consideration is only what eternal knowledge has attached to its attainment; this is the position of the people of truth. Other than this are the schools of the opponents, such as the school of al-Ka'bi from the Mu'tazila: that the slain is not dead because killing is the action of the servant, and death is the action of the Most High and the effect of His making, so the slain has two terms: killing and death, and that if he were not killed, he would live until his term which is death. And like the school of many of the Mu'tazila that the killer cut off the term of the slain, and that if he were not killed, he would live until an end which is his term that Allah knew he would die in if not for the killing, or he would die at that time. This is invalid, i.e., not corresponding to reality, because it contradicts the definitive proofs that do not accept interpretation, and everything invalid is not accepted by the rational people adhering to the truth. And fifty examples, and it is in Allah's knowledge restricted to his not doing, for example, a rising; and if he does it, he has sixty. And it preceded in His knowledge that he does it, so the increase over what is in the pages is an increase apparently.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. The author begins by asserting that the appointed term (ajal) is single and that the slain person dies exactly by that term, not by a separate death. This is based on Allah's eternal knowledge—whatever He knows will occur is what actually happens, as indicated by the Qur'anic verse (13:39) about erasing and confirming, with the Preserved Tablet being the source. This is the doctrine of Ahl al-Haqq. Then he presents the opposing Mu'tazilite views. First, the school of al-Ka'bi: the slain person is not considered dead by the term because killing is the servant's act and death is Allah's act, so the slain has two terms—one for being killed and one for natural death. Second, the view of many Mu'tazila: the killer cuts off the term, meaning if the slain were not killed, he would live until his original term. The author declares these invalid because they contradict definitive proofs that cannot be allegorically interpreted. He then mentions a related issue about deeds: a person may be destined to do fifty good deeds, but if he does an additional act (like rising early), he gets sixty; yet this is only in the apparent sense, as Allah's knowledge already includes the actual outcome. The conclusion is that all invalid views are rejected by rational people adhering to truth.

Key Terms
الأجل (al-ajal)
العلم الأزلي (al-'ilm al-azali)
أم الكتاب (Umm al-Kitab)
أهل الحق (Ahl al-Haqq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a slain person dies by a separate 'death' term, different from the term of his natural life.
Correction: The passage teaches that there is only one term for each person, and the slain person dies by that same term, because Allah's eternal knowledge encompasses all events.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for determining a person's term?
A) Human actions and choices
B) The eternal knowledge of Allah
C) The killer's intention
D) The person's age

Key Takeaway
Every person's death occurs by one fixed term decreed in Allah's eternal knowledge, not by any secondary cause.

Refuting Mu'tazilite Views on the Slain's Term
Refutation of two Mu'tazilite positions on the slain's term and an illustrative example on deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main Mu'tazilite objections to the single-term doctrine and why the author considers them invalid, as well as the illustrative example about deeds.

Core Idea
Mu'tazilite views on the slain's term contradict definitive proofs.

After establishing the Sunni position, the author addresses opposing views. He presents two Mu'tazilite schools and then dismisses them as contradictory to clear textual and rational proofs. The lesson also touches on a related matter about deeds and divine knowledge, showing that apparent increases in good deeds are only in the outward sense.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text that begins with 'وغير هذا من مذاهب المخالفين' and continues to the end. Identify the two Mu'tazilite positions and the author's response.
The last part about 'fifty examples' may seem separate; treat it as an additional clarification.
2
Analyze al-Ka'bi's argument
Al-Ka'bi claims the slain is not dead by the term because killing is the servant's act and death is Allah's act. He posits two terms.
Note the distinction between human and divine acts.
3
Analyze the majority Mu'tazilite view
Many Mu'tazilites say the killer cuts off the term; if not killed, the person would live until his natural term. The author rejects this.
4
Understand the refutation
The author declares both views invalid because they contradict 'definitive proofs' (al-qawati') that cannot be allegorically interpreted.
This is a strong dismissal based on methodological grounds.
5
Examine the deed example
The author mentions an example of fifty good deeds that can become sixty based on a condition. He clarifies that the increase is only apparent, as Allah's eternal knowledge already encompasses the outcome.
This reinforces the earlier point about divine knowledge.

Source Text

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly accept in your heart that every moment of your life—including its end—is already known to Allah and cannot be changed by anyone? If so, why do you sometimes fear or hope in people's actions more than in His decree?
?
When you hear of someone dying unexpectedly, does a part of you think, 'If only they had done something differently, they would be alive'? How does this passage challenge that thought, and what would it mean for you to surrender fully to Allah's comprehensive knowledge?
?
The Mu'tazilite view was appealing because it seemed to make sense of human responsibility. But the author calls it 'invalid' because it contradicts definitive proofs. Where in your life are you tempted to trust your own reasoning over clear revelation? Will you commit today to submitting to what Allah has made clear, even when it is difficult?

The Annihilation of the Soul at the First Trumpet Blast
The author presents the disagreement over whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast and cites evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement among scholars about whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast and the scriptural evidence cited for its annihilation.

Core Idea
The soul can be annihilated because it is corporeal, and everything corporeal perishes.

In this lesson, we examine a theological dispute regarding the fate of the soul at the first trumpet blast. The author presents the view of al-Subki, who favored the soul's survival, yet the passage emphasizes evidence that suggests the soul's annihilation. The discussion connects to the nature of the soul and its corporeality.

Guided Path
1
Understand the disagreement
Read the passage carefully and note that there is a difference of opinion on whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast. Al-Subki considered its survival as known.
The disagreement is about the soul's annihilation (fana) at the first blast.
2
Examine the evidence
The author cites two Qur'anic verses: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26) and 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (28:88) to support the possibility of annihilation.
These verses are used to argue that all corporeal beings undergo annihilation.
3
Interpret the poet's words
The passage includes a line from the poem: 'And regarding the necessity of the annihilation of the soul' which the author explains means the disappearance of its form as known from scripture at the first trumpet blast.
The poet uses 'fana al-nafs' to refer to the end of the soul's form.
4
Reflect on the nature of the soul
The argument relies on the soul being corporeal (jismiyya) because the term 'grasping' (qabd) implies physical holding, indicating corporeality. Anything corporeal is subject to annihilation.
Consider how the author links the concept of grasping to the soul's physicality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في فناء النفس والروح. وفي فنا النفس لدى النفخ اختلف واستظهر السبكي بقاها الذي عرف. ولما اختلف في هلاك الروح وفنائها عند النفخة الأولى أو استمرارها وبقائها .. ذكره لمناسبته لقبضها؛ لأن حقيقته المسك باليد، وهو مشعر بجسميتها، وكل جسم معرض للفناء قابل له، لقوله تعالى: ﴿كل من عليها فان﴾ و﴿كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه﴾، أشار إلى ذلك بقوله: (وفي) وجوب (فنا النفس) أي: ذهاب صورتها سمعا (لدى) أي: عند (النفخ) الأول الصادر من إسرافيل في الصور، وهو الناقور الذي يجمع الله فيه الأرواح، المشتمل على ثقب بعددها، وهذه النفخة الأولى
The discussion on the annihilation of the soul and spirit. And regarding the annihilation of the soul at the trumpet blast, there is disagreement, and al-Subki considered its survival as known. And when there was disagreement about the perishing of the spirit and its annihilation at the first trumpet blast or its continuation and survival... he mentioned it due to its suitability to its grasping; because its reality is holding with the hand, and it indicates its corporeality, and every body is subject to annihilation and receptive to it, due to His saying: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' and 'Everything is perishing except His Face.' He indicated that by his saying: (And regarding) the necessity of (annihilation of the soul) i.e., the disappearance of its form scripturally (at) i.e., at (the first trumpet blast) emanating from Israfil in the horn, which is the naqur in which Allah collects the spirits, comprising holes equal to their number, and this is the first blast.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a presentation of a theological disagreement and its supporting proof. The author begins by stating the topic: the annihilation (fana) of the soul (nafs) and spirit (ruh) at the first trumpet blast. He notes that there is a disagreement (ikhtilaf) and that al-Subki (a Shafi'i scholar) leaned toward the view of the soul's survival (baqa) from what is known. The author explains that this discussion is relevant to the concept of 'grasping' (qabd) of the soul, because the literal meaning of grasping is taking with the hand, which suggests that the soul has a corporeal nature (jismiyya). Anything corporeal is subject to annihilation. He cites Qur'anic verses as proof: Surah al-Rahman (26) and Surah al-Qasas (88) that everything perishes except Allah. The author then interprets the poet's words: 'And regarding the necessity of the annihilation of the soul' meaning the disappearance of its form as known from scriptural evidence (sam'an) at the first trumpet blast, which is the horn (sur) blown by the angel Israfil. This horn, called naqur, has holes equal to the number of souls, and Allah collects the spirits in it. This first blast causes the annihilation of all souls. The passage thus outlines the debate and gives scriptural basis for the possibility of annihilation.

Key Terms
فناء النفس (fana' al-nafs)
النفخة الأولى (al-nafkha al-ula)
السبكي (al-Subki)
القبض (al-qabd)
الناقور (al-naqur)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the soul is purely immaterial and cannot be annihilated.
Correction: The text shows the soul can be annihilated because it has corporeal aspects, as indicated by the term 'grasping' and the evidence that every body undergoes annihilation.

Checkpoint
Which verse is cited as evidence that the soul can be annihilated?
A) 'And with Him is the Mother of the Book'
B) 'Everyone upon it is perishing'
C) 'Allah eliminates what He wills and establishes'
D) 'And the earth will shine with the light of its Lord'

Key Takeaway
The soul's annihilation at the first trumpet blast is supported by its corporeal nature and Qur'anic proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the soul can be annihilated at the first blast, what does that tell you about the reality of your own existence? Are you living as if your soul could be taken at any moment?
?
The grasping (qabd) of the soul shows it is held by Allah. Do you truly feel that your soul is in His hand, and how would that certainty change the way you face your fears today?
?
Everything except Allah will perish. What are you clinging to that you have not surrendered to Him? If the trumpet sounds now, would your soul be ready to return to its Lord?

Falsity of Claiming Death at a Specific Time
States that the claim of death at that time if not killed is false.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that if not killed, a person would have died at that same time is considered false in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
Definitive proofs cannot be overridden by hypothetical claims.

In the section on sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation), the author addresses a specific hypothetical claim: that if a person were not killed, they would have died at that exact time anyway. This passage explains why such a claim is rejected. The reasoning hinges on the concept of qawati' (definitive proofs) which are not open to reinterpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the English translation. Note the key terms: sam'iyyat, bāṭil, qawāṭi‘, ta’wīl.
The Arabic is concise; let the translation guide you.
2
Identify the claim and its rejection
The passage states that the claim (that if not killed, he would have died at that time) is false. Why? Because it contradicts definitive proofs (al-qawāṭi‘).
3
Understand the consequence
The passage concludes that such falsehood is not accepted by rational people adhering to truth. Reflect on the importance of definitive proofs in Islamic theology.
This shows the authority of qawāṭi‘ in theological reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات لولا القتل، أو لماتَ في ذلك الوقت باطلٌ، أي: غير مطابق للواقع؛ لمنافاته القواطع التي لا تقبلُ التَّأويل، وكلُّ باطل لا يُقْبَلُ عند العُقلاء المتمسكين بالحق.
Section on sam'iyyat: If not for killing, or [if it were said] he would have died at that time, it is false, i.e., not corresponding to reality, because it contradicts the definitive proofs that do not accept interpretation, and every falsehood is not accepted by rational people adhering to the truth.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage states a rule in the section on sam'iyyat. It declares that the claim that if a person were not killed, he would have died at that specific time is false. The reason given is that it contradicts definitive proofs (qawati') which cannot be reinterpreted. Such a false statement is rejected by rational people who adhere to truth. The passage is a brief but definitive judgment.

Key Terms
سمعيات
باطل
قواطع
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the time of death is absolute and predetermined, so any claim about what would have happened is irrelevant.
Correction: This passage teaches that hypothetical claims that contradict definitive textual proofs are invalid.

Checkpoint
Why is the claim that if not killed the person would have died at that time considered false according to this passage?
A) Because it denies Allah's power
B) Because it contradicts the definitive proofs that do not accept interpretation
C) Because killing is never predetermined
D) Because the person would have lived forever

Key Takeaway
A claim that contradicts definitive proofs is automatically false and rejected by rational truth-seekers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever used a 'what if' scenario to avoid accepting a clear command from Allah, convincing yourself that circumstances would change the ruling? What would it cost you to submit to the definitive proof instead of the hypothetical?
?
The lesson states that every falsehood is rejected by rational people adhering to the truth. Is there a false belief you still hold because it comforts you, even though you know it contradicts what Allah has clearly revealed? Will you put it aside today?
?
When you face a difficult truth from the Qur’an or Sunnah, do you try to reinterpret it (ta’wīl) to make it easier, or do you accept it as a definitive proof? Which approach leads to true faith?

Disagreement on Annihilation of the Soul at First Trumpet Blast
Disagreement on annihilation of soul at first blast; as-Subki's preference for survival.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement about whether the soul is annihilated at the first trumpet blast and why as-Subki preferred the view of its continued existence.

Core Idea
The soul does not perish with the body; its annihilation at the first blast is disputed, but the preferred view is its survival.

This lesson examines a specific eschatological issue: does the soul cease to exist at the first trumpet blast? The Jawharah al-Tawhid cites disagreement and notes that Imam as-Subki favored the soul's continuation. We will explore the arguments on both sides presented in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the poetic line from the Jawharah and the extended commentary.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Find the group that holds obligatory annihilation based on the verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' and the group that holds its impossibility at that time.
Note the scriptural basis for each.
3
Understand exceptions and the soul-body distinction
See the exceptions (four archangels, houris, Musa) and the clarification that the soul is distinct from the body and not subject to its annihilation.
This distinguishes between death of the body and annihilation of the soul.
4
Note as-Subki's preferred position
Understand that as-Subki favored the soul's continued existence, which aligns with the well-known Sunni position.
This resolution preserves the soul's immortality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في فناء النفس والروح
٩- وفي فنا النفس لدى النفح اختلف واستظهر السبكي بقاها الذي عرف

ولما اختلف في هلاك الروح وفنائها عند النفخة الأولى أو استمرارها وبقائها.. ذكره لمناسبته لقبضها; لأن حقيقته المسك باليد، وهو مشعر بجسميتها، وكل جسم معرض للفناء قابل له، لقوله تعالى: «كل من عليها فان» [الرحمن: ٢٦]، «كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه» [القصص: ٨٨]، أشار إلى ذلك بقوله: (وفي) وجوب (فنا النفس)، أي: ذهاب صورتها سمعا (لدى) أي: عند (النفخ) الأول الصادر من إسرافيل في الصور، وهو الناقور الذي يجمع الله فيه الأرواح، المشتمل على ثقب بعددها، وهذه النفخة الأولى نفخة الفناء، لا يبقى عندها حي إلا مات، ولا حادث إلا هلك، إلا من شاء الله، كالملائكة الأربع الرؤساء، والحور العين، وموسى صعق في الدنيا مرة فجوزي بها (اختلف)، أي: اختلف العلماء; فذهب إلى الحكم بوجوب فنائها عند النفخ الأول طائفة لظاهر قوله تعالى: «كل من عليها فان» [الرحمن: ٢٦]، وذهب طائفة إلى امتناعه عليها عند ذلك، أما قبله وبعد الموت فلا خلاف بين المسلمين في بقائها منعمة إن كانت من أهل الخير، أو معذبة إن كانت من أهل الشر، وفناء البدن لا يوجب فناء النفس المغايرة له، وكونها مدبرة له متصرفة فيه لا يقتضي فنائها بفنائه. (واستظهر) الإمام أبو الحسن تقي الدين علي بن عبد الكافي (السبكي) من هذا الخلاف (بقاها) أي: القول باستمرار البقاء (الذي عرف).
Discussion on the annihilation of the soul and spirit: 9- And regarding the annihilation of the soul at the blast, they differed, and as-Subki favored its continuation which is known. When they differed about the destruction of the spirit and its annihilation at the first blast or its continuity and permanence, he mentioned it for its appropriateness to its seizure; because its reality is grasping by the hand, and it suggests its corporeality, and every body is subject to annihilation and susceptible to it, due to His statement: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [55:26], 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [28:88]. He pointed to that by his saying: (And concerning the obligatory annihilation of the soul (fana an-nafs), meaning the disappearance of its form according to revelation, (at) i.e., at the (first blast) emanating from Israfil into the Trumpet, which is the naqur in which Allah gathers the souls, containing a hole for each of them. This first blast is the blast of annihilation; no living thing remains but dies, and no event but perishes, except whom Allah wills, like the four archangels, the houris, and Musa who was struck unconscious in the world once and was recompensed with it. (They differed), i.e., the scholars differed. One group went to the judgment of its obligatory annihilation at the first blast due to the apparent meaning of His statement 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [55:26]. Another group went to its impossibility at that time. As for before that and after death, there is no disagreement among Muslims that it remains, enjoying bliss if it was of the people of good, or punished if it was of the people of evil. The annihilation of the body does not necessitate the annihilation of the soul, which is different from it, and its being a manager and controller of the body does not entail its annihilation by its annihilation. (And as-Subki favored) the Imam Abu al-Hasan Taqi ad-Din Ali ibn Abd al-Kafi as-Subki, from this disagreement, (its continuation) i.e., the opinion of the permanence of existence (which is known).
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the disagreement regarding the annihilation of the soul (nafs) and spirit (ruh) at the first trumpet blast. It begins by citing the poetic line from the Jawharah which states the existence of a difference of opinion and that as-Subki preferred its continuation. The commentator then explains: the reason for mentioning it here is its connection to the 'qabd' (seizing) of the soul, which implies corporeality, and every body is susceptible to annihilation. He cites verses from the Quran to support the possibility of annihilation. Then he defines the first blast as the blast of annihilation (nafkh al-fana') where all except whom Allah wills die. He mentions exceptions: the four archangels, the houris, and Musa (who was already stunned in this world). He then states that scholars disagreed: one group argued for obligatory annihilation based on the apparent meaning of the verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing', while another group argued that annihilation is impossible at that time. He clarifies that before the blast and after death, there is no dispute that the soul remains, experiencing bliss or punishment. He emphasizes that the annihilation of the body does not necessitate the annihilation of the soul because the soul is different and is a manager of the body. Finally, he states that as-Subki favored the opinion of the soul's continued existence (baqa') at the first blast, which is the well-known position of Ahl al-Haqq.

Key Terms
فناء النفس
النفخ الأول
بقاء النفس
السبكي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul perishes with the body at death or at the first blast and ceases to exist entirely.
Correction: The soul is a distinct substance that continues after bodily death and, according to the preferred opinion, also survives the first trumpet blast.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the basis for the group that holds the obligatory annihilation of the soul at the first blast?
A) The verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face'
B) The verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing'
C) The fact that the body perishes
D) The opinion of as-Subki

Key Takeaway
The soul's annihilation at the first blast is not obligatory; the preferred view is its continued existence, aligning with the principle that the soul is distinct from the body and not subject to its annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The soul, unlike the body, will not necessarily perish at the first blast. If you truly believed that your soul will outlast every physical thing you own, how would you change your priorities today? What would you invest more in: your body or your soul?
?
When you imagine standing before your Lord after the trumpet blast, your soul either in bliss or punishment because of deeds done in this life—does that reality frighten you enough to change one habit this week? Which one?
?
The scholars agree that before the blast and after death, the soul remains, experiencing reward or punishment. Are you living as if that is true? Or do your daily actions reveal that you act as if this life is all there is?

The Soul's Annihilation at the First Trumpet Blast
Debate on the soul's survival at the first trumpet blast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two major scholarly opinions on whether the soul perishes at the first trumpet blast, and the evidence for the view that it survives.

Core Idea
The soul is distinct from the body and survives the trumpet blast, as per the preferred view of Ahl al-Haqq.

This passage addresses a key question in Islamic eschatology: does the human soul perish at the first trumpet blast like the body? The author presents two contrasting opinions, then argues for the survival of the soul based on scriptural indications and rational principles. By the end, you will see how Imam al-Subki’s reasoning using istishab (presumption of continuity) leads to the chosen view.

Guided Path
1
Context of the First Blast
Read the opening lines describing the blast and its universal effect, with exceptions. Notice the scope of annihilation.
The blast is called 'Nafkhat al-Fana' — the blast of annihilation.
2
The Two Opinions
Identify the two groups: one says the soul must perish (based on Qur'an 55:26), the other says it is impossible. Understand their scriptural basis.
3
Consensus Before and After
Note the agreement that before the blast and after death, the soul persists in felicity or punishment. This sets a baseline.
The body's annihilation does not imply the soul's annihilation.
4
Al-Subki's Argument
Follow al-Subki's reasoning: he infers survival from post-death consensus and invokes istishab — the principle that a persistent state continues until evidence changes it.
Istishab is a key legal maxim applied here to theology.
5
Conclusion and Exception
See that the preferred view considers the soul among those excepted in Qur'an 27:87, meaning it does not perish at the blast.
This aligns with the view of Ahl al-Haqq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في فناء النفس والروح نفخة الفناء لا يبقى عندها حي إلا مات، ولا حادث إلا هلك، إلا من شاء الله، كالملائكة الأربع الرؤساء، والحور العين، وموسى صعق في الدنيا مرة فجوزي بها (اختلف)، أي: اختلف العلماء؛ فذهب إلى الحكم بوجوب فنائها عند النفخ الأول طائفة لظاهر قوله تعالى: {كل من عليها فان} [الرحمن: 26]، وذهب طائفة إلى امتناعه عليها عند ذلك، أما قبله وبعد الموت فلا خلاف بين المسلمين في بقائها منعمة إن كانت من أهل الخير، أو معذبة إن كانت من أهل الشر، وفناء البدن لا يوجب فناء النفس المغايرة له، وكونها مدبرة له متصرفة فيه لا يقتضي فنائها بفنائه. واستظهر الإمام أبو الحسن تقي الدين علي بن عبد الكافي السبكي من هذا الخلاف بقاها، أي: القول باستمرار البقاء الذي عهد سابقا، قال: لأنهم اتفقوا على بقائها بعد الموت لسؤالها في القبر وجوابها وتنعيمها أو تعذيبها فيه، والأصل في كل باق استمراره حتى يظهر ما يصرف عنه، وما قاله السبكي هو المختار عند أهل الحق؛ فتكون من المستثنى بقوله تعالى: {إلا من شاء الله} [النمل: 87].
The discussion on the annihilation of the soul and spirit: the blast of annihilation, no living thing remains upon it except it dies, and no contingent thing except it perishes, except whom Allah wills, such as the four chief angels, the houris, and Moses—he was struck unconscious in the world once and was recompensed for it. (They disagreed): that is, the scholars disagreed. For one group went to the ruling that its annihilation at the first blast is obligatory due to the apparent meaning of His statement: {Every soul upon it will perish} [Ar-Rahman: 26]. And another group went to the impossibility of annihilation upon it at that time. As for before it and after death, there is no disagreement among the Muslims that it remains—felicitated if it was of the people of good, or punished if it was of the people of evil. The annihilation of the body does not necessitate the annihilation of the soul, which is other than it, and its being a manager and disposer for the body does not entail its annihilation by the annihilation of the body. And Imam Abu Al-Hasan Taqi al-Din Ali ibn Abd al-Kafi al-Subki adopted from this disagreement its survival, i.e., the statement of the continuation of survival—that which was known previously. He said: because they agreed upon its survival after death due to its being questioned in the grave and its answer and its being felicitated or punished therein. And the principle regarding every persistent thing is its continuation until something appears that turns it away. And what al-Subki said is the chosen view with the people of truth; thus it is among those excepted by His statement: {Except whom Allah wills} [An-Naml: 87].
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal argument about whether the human soul perishes at the first trumpet blast (Nafkhat al-Fana') before the resurrection. The author begins by stating the topic: discussion on the annihilation of the soul and spirit. He describes the blast as causing the death of every living thing and the perishing of every contingent thing, with exceptions such as the four archangels, the houris, and Moses—who had been struck unconscious in the world and was recompensed. Then he reports the scholarly disagreement (ikhtilaf): a group holds that the soul must perish at the first blast, citing the verse 'Everything on it will perish' (Ar-Rahman 26). Another group holds that the soul does not perish at that time. He clarifies that before the blast and after death, all Muslims agree that the soul remains, either in bliss or punishment. He then argues that the perishing of the body does not necessitate the perishing of the soul, since the soul is distinct from the body and merely manages it. He then presents the view of Imam al-Subki, who favored the persistence of the soul. Al-Subki reasons that there is consensus on the soul's survival after death (based on its questioning and reward/punishment in the grave) and invokes the principle of istishab (presumption of continuity): anything that persists continues until evidence shows otherwise. Therefore, al-Subki's view is the chosen one of Ahl al-Haqq, making the soul among those excepted in the verse 'except whom Allah wills' (An-Naml 87).

Key Terms
فناء النفس
نفخة الفناء
بقاء النفس
السبكي
استصحاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the soul perishes with the body at the first trumpet blast.
Correction: The passage argues the soul is a distinct substance that continues after the body's death and even after the first trumpet blast, based on consensus and istishab.

Checkpoint
What is the chosen view of Ahl al-Haqq regarding the soul at the first trumpet blast?
A) The soul must perish with the body.
B) The soul remains and does not perish.
C) The soul is annihilated and then recreated.
D) The soul is uncertain.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Subki's use of istishab and consensus leads to the conclusion that the soul survives the first trumpet blast, making it an exception in the Qur'anic verse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage teaches that your soul is not annihilated with your body. If you truly believed that your soul—your very self—will continue to exist and be held accountable after the trumpet blast, how would your priorities today change? What would you start doing differently this week?
?
Al-Subki argued that the soul's survival is the default state, and nothing has overturned that default. Have you been living as if the soul's existence is fragile or temporary? What would it mean for your relationship with Allah to act on the certainty that your soul is ongoing and its fate is being determined right now?
?
The soul is distinct from the body; it manages the body but is not dependent on it. Are you feeding your soul with what sustains it for its eternal journey, or are you so absorbed in bodily concerns that you neglect the very thing that will live on? Name one specific way you will nourish your soul today.

The Coccyx Bone: Seed of Resurrection
Explains the survival of the coccyx as basis for resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the coccyx bone remains undecayed as the physical basis for bodily resurrection, as affirmed by Sunni creed.

Core Idea
The coccyx bone never decays, serving as Allah's seed for resurrection.

This lesson examines a specific element of Sunni eschatology: the survival of the coccyx bone ('ajb al-dhanab). The passage presents a theological dispute about whether this bone perishes, and settles it with a hadith from the two Sahihs. Understanding this doctrine reinforces the belief in bodily resurrection as a physical reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to grasp the core claim and supporting hadith.
Notice the poetic opening line and how it introduces the topic.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage mentions a disagreement about whether the coccyx perishes or survives. Identify both views and note which is more famous.
The famous opinion is that it does not perish.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith from Bukhari and Muslim is quoted as proof. Understand that this hadith directly states that every human part decays except one bone, the coccyx.
This hadith is the primary textual evidence for the doctrine.
4
Connect to resurrection
Reflect on why this matters: the undecayed coccyx is the seed from which Allah re-creates the body on the Day of Judgment.
This doctrine affirms the physicality of the afterlife.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بقاء عجب الذنب من الإنسان المزني للبلى ووضعا - عجب الذنب كالروح لكن صححا ومما يناسب هذا الخلاف قوله: (عجب الذنب) اختلف في فنائه وبقائه (كالروح) على قولين مشهورهما أيضا أنه لا يفنى؛ لحديث الصحيحين: ليس من الإنسان شيء إلا يبلى، إلا عظما واحدا، وهو عجب الذنب.
The survival of the coccyx bone from the human being: Al-Muzani [said] for decay and clarified - the coccyx is like the soul, but he corrected. And among what suits this disagreement is his statement: (the coccyx) they differed regarding its annihilation and its survival (like the soul) upon two opinions, the most famous of which is that it does not perish; due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'There is nothing of the human being that does not decay except one bone, and that is the coccyx.'
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal exposition on the survival of the coccyx bone ('ajb al-dhanab) as the foundation for bodily resurrection. It begins with a poetic verse: 'Al-Muzani clarified for decay, and he explained - the coccyx is like the soul, but he corrected.' The commentator then explains that, similar to the soul, there is a disagreement about whether the coccyx perishes or remains. The more famous opinion is that it does not perish, supported by the hadith from the two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim) which states that every part of the human decays except one bone—the coccyx. This bone is understood to be the seed from which the body is resurrected on the Day of Judgment. The passage thus affirms the physical basis for bodily resurrection, a key tenet of Sunni eschatology.

Correction: The hadith clarifies that the coccyx bone does not decay, serving as the seed for resurrection.

The Debate on the Permanence of the Coccyx
Sanusi contrasts two scholarly views on the annihilation of the coccyx.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly opinions on whether the coccyx (ʿajab al-dhanab) remains after death, and the scriptural evidence each side uses.

Core Idea
The coccyx: a small bone that sparks a big debate on resurrection.

This lesson examines a fascinating point of theological disagreement: does the coccyx—a tiny bone at the base of the spine—perish or remain after death? The issue touches on resurrection, bodily continuity, and interpretation of scriptural evidence. Let's explore the views and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the use of hadith and Quranic quotation.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents two views: the more famous view that the coccyx does not perish, and the view of al-Muzani that it does perish. Find the evidence each side uses.
3
Understand the reasoning
See how the majority relies on the explicit hadith, while al-Muzani relies on the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse. Note the author's clarification about the comparison to the soul.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يناسب هذا الخلاف قوله: (عَجْبُ الذَّنَب) اختلف في فنائه وبقائه (كَالرُّوحِ) على قولين مشهورُهُما أيضا أنه لا يفنى؛ لحديث الصحيحين: «ليس من الإنسان شيء إِلَّا يبلى، إِلَّا عظمًا واحدًا، وهو عَجْبُ الذنب، منه خَلْقُ الخلق يوم القيامة»، وعند مسلم بلفظ: «كل ابن آدم يأكله التراب إِلَّا عجب الذنب، منه خُلق، ومنه يُركَّب». وهو عظم كالخردلة في العصعص آخر سلسلة الظهر، مختص بالإنسان كمغرز الذنب للدابة. التشبيه لا بقيد وقت النفخ. (لَكِنْ صَحَّحَا) الإمام إسماعيل بن يحيى (المُزَنِيُّ) نسبةً لمُزَيْنَة قبيلة من كلب (للبلى)، أي: الفناء، تمشكا بظاهر قوله تعالى: ﴿كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ﴾؛ لأن فناء الكل يستلزم فناء عجب الذنب.
And among what suits this disagreement is his saying: 'ʿAjab al-Dhanab (coccyx) – there is disagreement concerning its annihilation and its permanence, like the soul – on two sayings, the more famous of which is also that it does not perish, due to the hadith of the two Sahihs: 'There is nothing of the son of Adam that does not decay except one bone, and that is the coccyx; from it the creation is made on the Day of Resurrection.' And in Muslim: 'Every son of Adam is eaten by the earth except the coccyx; from it he was created, and from it he is composed.' And it is a bone like a mustard seed in the coccyx at the end of the spinal column, specific to humans like the stub of the tail for the beast. The comparison (of the coccyx to the soul) is not restricted to the time of the Blast. 'But al-Muzani affirmed' – Imam Ismaʿil ibn Yahya al-Muzani, of the tribe of Muzayna from Kalb – 'annihilation', i.e., perishing, clinging to the apparent meaning of His saying: 'Everyone upon it (the earth) will perish' [55:26], because the perishing of everything entails the perishing of the coccyx.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage discusses the different scholarly opinions about whether the coccyx (ʿajab al-dhanab) remains after death or perishes. The author begins by noting that this issue is relevant to the earlier disagreement about the soul. There are two views, and the more famous one is that the coccyx does not perish, based on the authentic hadith from Bukhari and Muslim stating that every part of a human decays except this one bone, which is the origin from which the body will be recreated on the Day of Resurrection. The author then describes the coccyx as a small bone in the lower back, like a mustard seed, unique to humans. He clarifies that the comparison of the coccyx to the soul (in the poetic line) concerns only the dispute over permanence and annihilation, not the timing of the Trumpet Blast. Then he mentions Imam al-Muzani, who held the opposite view: the coccyx does perish. Al-Muzani based his opinion on the apparent meaning of Quran 55:26, 'Everyone upon it will perish,' arguing that this universal statement includes the coccyx as part of the human body. Thus, he insisted on the annihilation of this bone, contrary to the hadith-based majority view.

Key Terms
عجب الذنب
الروح
المزني
البلى
الفناء
الخلق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the coccyx is the only part of the body that never decays as an eternal physical remnant.
Correction: The hadith speaks of the coccyx as the seed from which the body is recreated (like a seed), not an eternal remnant that persists forever without change.

Checkpoint

A) Quran 55:26
B) The hadith from the Sahihayn
C) Consensus of the Companions
D) Analogical reasoning

Key Takeaway
The coccyx debate illustrates how kalam scholars weigh hadith and Quranic verses in resolving a question about bodily resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

When you face conflicting evidences in your own life, do you cling to the clear text that comforts you or the one that challenges your assumptions? Take one minute to write down a verse that you have been avoiding applying.
?

The Survival of the Coccyx Bone: Evidence, Objection, and Resolution
Discussion of the coccyx bone's survival, Muzani's objection, and the preferred view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments for the survival of the coccyx bone, al-Muzani's objection based on the Quranic verse, and the stronger view that it remains as a devotional matter.

Core Idea
The coccyx bone survives as a sign for resurrection, despite Muzani's objection from the Quran.

This passage enters the sam'iyyat section, dealing with eschatological matters known only through revelation. The survival of the coccyx bone (عجب الذنب) is a well-known hadith, but theologians like al-Muzani raised a strong objection from the Quran. We will see how later scholars reconciled the hadith with the verse and why the stronger opinion maintains the bone's survival as a devotional matter.

Guided Path
1
Discover the hadith and description of the coccyx bone
Read the passage noting the hadith from Bukhari and Muslim regarding the bone that does not decay. Understand its location and function.
The bone is like a mustard seed at the base of the spine.
2
Analyze al-Muzani's objection
Al-Muzani argued that the Quranic verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' necessitates the annihilation of every part, including the coccyx. Understand his use of the whole-part argument.
He claimed the hadith only says it is not eaten by earth, not that it is not annihilated by other means.
3
Examine the reconciliation
See how al-Muzani's followers reconciled his view: God annihilates the body by earth, then the bone by another means, similar to the death of the Angel of Death.
This interpretation does not contradict the hadith.
4
Grasp the stronger view
The author states the stronger view is that the bone never decays, its survival is devotional, and some scholars explained it as a sign for angels for resurrection.
This view is based on the apparent meaning of the hadith.

بقاءُ عَجْبِ الذَّنَبِ مِن الإِنسان
الذنب ، مِنه خَلْقُ الخَلقِ  َيومَ القيامة، وعند مسلم بلفظ: «كل ابن آدم يأكله التُّرَاب إِلَّا عَجب الذنب، منه خُلق، ومنه يُركَّب، وهو عَظمُ كالخَرْدَلَة في العُصْعُص آخرَ سِلسلة الظهر، مُختص بالإنسان كمِغرز الذنب للدابة. والتشبيه لا بقيد وقتِ النَّفخ. (لَكِنْ صَحَّحَا) الإمام إسماعيل بن يحيى (المُزَنِيُّ) نسبةً لمُزَيْنَة قبيلةٌ مِن كلب (للبلي)، أي: الفناء، تمشكا بظاهر قوله تعالى: ﴿كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانِ ﴾ [الرحمن: ٢٦] ؛ لأنَّ فناء الكل يستلزم فناء الجزء. 
قسم السمعيات فناء الجزء (وَوَضَّحَا)، أي: بيَّن صحة ما ذهب إليه بتأويله دليل الأول بما حاصله : أنَّه يجوز أن يُفني الله الإنسانَ بالتراب، فإذا لم يبق إِلَّا عَجْبُ الذَّنب أفناه الله تعالى بلا تُرابِ، كما يميتُ ملك الموت بلا مَلَكِ مَوْتٍ، ولا يُشكل عليه حديث مسلم الآخر: «إنَّ في الإنسان عظما لا تأكله الأرض أبدًا»، لأنَّه ليس فيه تعرّض إلَّا لعدم فنائه بالأرض، والمزني يقول به، ووافقه ابن قتيبة وقال : إنَّه آخر ما يبلى مِن الميّت، ولم يتعرضا لوقت فنائه، هل هو عند فناء العالم أو قبل ذلك ؟ وهو محتمل . 
والأقوى فى النَّظر : أنَّه لا يبلى ؛ لظاهر الحديث ، وبقائه تعبدي، وإنْ علله بعضهم بجواز كونه جُعِلَ علامةً للملائكة على إحياء كُلَّ إنسانٍ بجواهره كانت في الدُّنيا بأعيانها ، ولولاه لجَوَّزَتِ الملائكةُ إعادة الأرواح إلى أبدانِ غيْرها .
The survival of the coccyx bone of the human. The tailbone, from it is the creation of creation on the Day of Resurrection, and according to Muslim in wording: 'Every son of Adam the earth eats except the coccyx bone, from it he was created, and from it he is assembled, and it is a bone like a mustard seed in the coccyx at the end of the spinal column, specific to humans like the insertion of the tail for an animal. And the comparison is not restricted to the time of the blast. But al-Muzani affirmed (annihilation), Imam Isma'il ibn Yahya al-Muzani, attributed to Muzayna, a tribe from Kalb, (al-bila), meaning annihilation, clinging to the apparent meaning of His statement: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' [ar-Rahman 26]; because the annihilation of the whole necessitates the annihilation of the part. Section of sam'iyyat: annihilation of the part. And they clarified, i.e., he explained the correctness of what he went to by interpreting the proof of the first with its summary: that it is permissible that God annihilates the human by earth, then when nothing remains except the coccyx bone, God annihilates it without earth, just as He causes the Angel of Death to die without an angel of death. And it is not problematic for it the other hadith of Muslim: 'Indeed in man there is a bone that the earth never eats,' because it only addresses its not being annihilated by earth, and al-Muzani says with it, and Ibn Qutayba agreed with him and said: It is the last thing that decays from the dead, and they did not address the time of its annihilation, whether it is at the annihilation of the world or before that? And it is probable. And the strongest in consideration: that it does not decay; due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, and its survival is devotional, although some have given the reason that it is made a sign for the angels for the revival of every human with their substances that were in the world in their very identities, and without it the angels would allow the return of spirits to bodies other than theirs.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage discusses the controversial issue of the survival of the 'coccyx bone' (عجب الذنب) after death, which is relevant to the bodily resurrection. It begins by citing the well-known hadith in Bukhari and Muslim stating that every part of the human body decays except this bone, and from it the body is recreated on the Day of Resurrection. The bone is described as small, like a mustard seed, located at the base of the spine, and is unique to humans. The commentator notes that the comparison (of the bone to the spirit) is not restricted to the time of the blast. Then the objection of Imam al-Muzani is presented: he held that everything, including this bone, must be annihilated completely, based on the Quranic verse 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (ar-Rahman 26), arguing that the annihilation of the whole (all created beings) necessitates the annihilation of every part. The commentator then explains how al-Muzani's followers reconciled his view with the hadith: they said that God first annihilates the human body by the earth, and when only the coccyx remains, He annihilates it by a different means (not by earth), just as the Angel of Death is made to die without any other angel. This interpretation does not contradict the hadith that says the earth does not eat the bone, because that hadith only denies annihilation by earth, not annihilation by other means. Ibn Qutayba agreed with al-Muzani, stating that this bone is merely the last part of the body to decay. However, the commentator states that the stronger opinion (الأقوى في النظر) is that the bone never decays at all, based on the apparent meaning of the hadith. Its preservation is considered a devotional matter (تعبدي), though some scholars have suggested a wisdom behind it: that it serves as a sign for the angels when they are tasked with resurrecting each individual with the exact same material substance they had in the world, preventing confusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the hadith about the bone not being consumed by earth implies it can never be annihilated at all.
Correction: Al-Muzani clarifies it only means it is not annihilated by earth, not that it cannot be annihilated by other means.

Checkpoint
According to the stronger view presented in the passage, why does the coccyx bone survive?
A) Because it is made of an indestructible material.
B) Because its survival is a devotional matter and it serves as a sign for the angels.
C) Because God cannot annihilate it.
D) Because it will be annihilated at the end of time.

Key Takeaway
The survival of the coccyx bone is affirmed by hadith, and despite Muzani's objection from the Quran, the stronger view holds it survives as a devotional sign for resurrection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely believe that your physical body will be resurrected, including bones that have decayed? If you doubt, which piece of evidence—the hadith or the Quranic verse—shakes your certainty, and why?
?
The coccyx bone is a hidden sign of Allah's power to resurrect. In your daily life, do you notice any other signs in your own body that point to the afterlife? If not, what keeps you from seeing them?
?
If you were in the position of the angels tasked with resurrecting billions of people with identical substances, how would you ensure each soul returns to the right body? Does the idea that Allah provides a sign like the coccyx bone change your trust in His justice and ability?

The Survival of the Tailbone and Its Annihilation by God
Commentary explains the survival of the tailbone and its annihilation by God.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological reasoning regarding the survival of the 'ajb al-dhanab and its annihilation by God, and how it serves as the basis for bodily resurrection.

Core Idea
The tailbone's survival is devotional and not contradicted by hadith; it serves as a sign for resurrection.

This lesson explores the commentary on the survival of the tailbone ('ajb al-dhanab) as the basis for resurrection. The author clarifies the proof that God annihilates everything except this bone, which is only impervious to earth, not to God's power. We will examine the hadith and the reasoning behind the stronger view that it never decays.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the author's argumentative flow.
The passage is dense with theological reasoning; focus on the main thread.
2
Understand the proof: annihilation by earth then by God without earth
The author argues that God first annihilates the human by earth, leaving only the tailbone, then annihilates the tailbone without earth. This parallels the death of the Angel of Death.
This shows God's absolute power over all creation.
3
Address the hadith objection
The hadith stating a bone will never be consumed by earth only negates annihilation by earth, not by other means. Thus it does not conflict with the proof.
Al-Muzani and Ibn Qutaybah agreed the tailbone is the last to decay but didn't specify final annihilation.
4
Grasp the stronger view and its rationale
The stronger view is that the tailbone never decays, based on the apparent meaning of the hadith, and its survival is devotional (ta'abbudi). It serves as a sign for angels to ensure each human is resurrected with their exact original substances.
Without this sign, angels might mistakenly reunite souls with different bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات فناء الجزء (وَوَضَّحَا)، أي: بيَّن صحة ما ذهب إليه بتأويله دليل الأول بما حاصله : أنَّه يجوز أن يُفني الله الإنسانَ بالتراب ، فإذا لم يبق إِلَّا عَجْبُ الذَّنب أفناه الله تعالى بلا تُرابِ، كما يميت ملك الموت بلا مَلَكِ مَوْتٍ، ولا يُشكل عليه حديث مسلم الآخر: «إنَّ في الإنسان عظما لا تأكله الأرض أبدًا»، لأنَّه ليس فيه تعرّض إلَّا لعدم فنائه بالأرض، والمزني يقول به ، ووافقه ابن قتيبة وقال : إنَّه آخر ما يبلى مِن الميّت، ولم يتعرضا لوقت فنائه، هل هو عند فناء العالم أو قبل ذلك ؟ وهو محتمل . والأقوى فى النَّظر : أنَّه لا يبلى ؛ لظاهر الحديث ، وبقائه تعبدي ، وإنْ علله بعضهم بجواز كونه جُعِلَ علامةً للملائكة على إحياء كُلَّ إنسانٍ بجواهره كانت في الدُّنيا بأعيانها ، ولولاه لجَوَّزَتِ الملائكةُ إعادة الأرواح إلى أبدانِ غيْرها .
Section on sam'iyyat: The annihilation of the part (and he clarified), i.e., he explained the correctness of what he went to by interpreting the first proof, the summary of which: that it is permissible for God to annihilate the human by earth, and when nothing remains except the tailbone, God the Exalted annihilates it without earth, just as He causes the Angel of Death to die without an angel of death. And it is not problematic for him the other hadith of Muslim: 'Verily in the human there is a bone that the earth will never consume,' because it only refers to its non-annihilation by earth. Al-Muzani says with it, and Ibn Qutaybah agreed with him and said: It is the last thing that decays from the dead, and they did not address the time of its annihilation, whether it is at the annihilation of the world or before that? It is probable. And the stronger in consideration is that it does not decay, due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, and its remaining is devotional, though some explained it by the possibility that it is made a sign for the angels for reviving every human with their substances that were in this world as they are, and if not for it the angels would have permitted returning souls to other bodies.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is a commentary explaining the survival of the 'ajb al-dhanab (tailbone) as the basis for bodily resurrection. The author begins by clarifying the proof that it is permissible for God to first annihilate the human through earth, and when only the tailbone remains, He annihilates that as well without earth, citing an analogy with the death of the Angel of Death. The author then addresses an objection based on a hadith in Sahih Muslim stating that a bone in the human will never be consumed by the earth. He points out that this hadith only indicates non-annihilation by earth, not absolute non-annihilation, thus not conflicting with the possibility of annihilation by other means. He mentions that al-Muzani and Ibn Qutaybah held that the tailbone is the last to decay, but they did not specify the time of its final annihilation. The author then states that the stronger view is that it does not decay at all, due to the apparent meaning of the hadith, and its survival is devotional (ta'abbudi). He also cites an explanation: the tailbone is a sign for angels to know that each human is resurrected with his exact original substances; otherwise angels might mistakenly reunite souls with different bodies.

Key Terms
عَجْبُ الذَّنَب
تعبدي
فناء الجزء
سمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about the bone not being eaten by earth is sometimes taken as proof that it never perishes at all.
Correction: The author clarifies it only negates annihilation by earth, not by other means, so the bone can still be annihilated by God.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the stronger view regarding the tailbone?
A) It is annihilated at the time of the world's annihilation.
B) It does not decay at all, based on the apparent meaning of the hadith and it is devotional.
C) It is always annihilated by earth.
D) It is the first to decay from the dead.

Key Takeaway
The survival of the tailbone is a devotional matter and serves as a sign for angels to ensure each human is resurrected with their exact original substances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly trust that God will resurrect you with your exact substances, even if only a devotional sign remains? If so, why do you still fear death as if you might be lost?
?
The author says the tailbone's survival is a sign for angels, not for you. Yet you are the one being resurrected. Does this make you feel more or less certain of your personal resurrection? How does your heart respond to the idea that your identity is so precisely preserved by God?
?
The concept of ta'abbudi requires accepting matters without full empirical demonstration. In what areas of your life do you demand proof before submitting to God's commands? How can this lesson shape your willingness to accept other unseen truths?

Specifying the General Statement 'Everything is Perishing'
Commentary explains specification of the general verse and presents two interpretive approaches.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars reconcile the verse 'Everything is perishing' with the survival of the spirit and tailbone, and the two main interpretive approaches: specification (takhsīṣ) and reinterpretation (ma'nā al-imkān).

Core Idea
The Qur'anic 'everything perishes' is not absolute—scholars specify or reinterpret it to fit revealed truths.

This lesson addresses a key question: how can the verse 'Everything is perishing' (Qaṣaṣ 88) be reconciled with the belief that the spirit and tailbone endure? The poem and commentary present two scholarly responses: specification (takhṣīṣ) and reinterpretation of 'perishing' as 'liable to perish.' You will learn the definitions of general and specific, and see how later scholars offered an alternative that avoids specification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the problem
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the verse cited and the issue it raises given the belief in the survival of the spirit and tailbone.
The problem is an apparent contradiction between the general verse and specific hadith.
2
Understand the first solution: specification
The author explains that scholars specify the verse's generality, restricting it to exclude certain things. Learn the definitions of 'general' (al-ʿāmm) and 'specification' (al-takhṣīṣ).
Specification restricts a general term to some of its individuals.
3
Learn the second solution: reinterpretation
Later scholars denied any need for specification. They reinterpreted 'perishing' as 'liable to perish' due to contingency and need.
This avoids the need to specify the verse.
4
Compare the two approaches
Reflect on why later scholars preferred the reinterpretation. Both approaches are considered valid, but the latter is favored by verifiers for its coherence.
Think about the theological implications of each.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تخصيص عموم الهلاك ۹۲ - وكُلَّ شَيءٍ هالك قد خَصَّصُوا عُمُومَهُ فَاطْلُبْ لِمَا قَدْ لَخَصُوا (وَ) لمَّا كانَ القولُ ببقاء الرُّوحِ وعَجْبِ الذَّنب هو الرَّاجح ، أَجابَ عما يخالفه كقوله تعالى: (كُلُّ شَيءٍ مِنَ الكائنات جواهرها وأعراضها هَالِكُ ، أي: زائلٌ فَانٍ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ ﴾ [القصص: ۸۸]، أي: ذَاتَه ، مُقتضاه: أَنَّ كُلَّ ما سواه تعالى محكوم عليه بالهلاك ؛ لأنَّ الاستثناء معيار العموم ، وحاصل جوابه : أنَّ العلماءَ قَدْ خَصَّصُوا عُمُومَهُ أي : فَصَرُوا استغرَاقَه ؛ إذ التَّخصيصُ قَصْرُ العام على بعض أفراده، والعام: لفظ يَستغرِقُ الصَّالح له مِن غير حصر، (فَاطْلُبْ)، أي: توجه لِمَا قَدْ لَخَصُوا يعني الأمور الَّتي نَصُّوا عليها وَرَوَوْا أحاديثها ، وهذا الذي سلكه الناظم رحمه الله تعالى في الجواب لجماعة كابن عبّاس . وذهب محققو المتأخّرينَ إلى أنّه لا استثناء ولا تخصيص ، وأن معنى «هالك قابل للهلاك مِن حيثُ إمكانه وافتقاره، كما هو معنى «فَانٍ» أيضاً .
Specifying the generality of annihilation. 92 - And every thing is perishing; they have specified its generality, so seek what they have summarized. (And) since the statement of the survival of the spirit and the tailbone is the preponderant, he responded to what contradicts it, like His statement the Exalted: 'Everything of existents, their substances and their accidents, is perishing, i.e., vanishing, passing away, except His Face' — i.e., His Essence. Its implication is that everything other than the Exalted is judged subject to annihilation, because the exception is the criterion of generality. And the summary of his response: that the scholars have specified its generality, i.e., they limited its comprehensiveness; for specification is restricting the general to some of its individuals. And the general is an expression that comprehensively includes everything qualified for it without enumeration. (So seek) i.e., direct yourself to what they have summarized, meaning the matters that they have stipulated and narrated their hadiths. And this is what the poet, may God have mercy on him, adopted in the response for a group like Ibn 'Abbas. And the verifying scholars among the later scholars held that there is no exception nor specification, and that the meaning of 'perishing' is 'liable to perish' in terms of its possibility and need, just as is the meaning of 'vanishing' also.
Source pages p. 490

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the poetic line 'And every thing is perishing; they have specified its generality...' The author first states that since the view of the survival of the spirit and the tailbone is preponderant, a response is given to the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' (Qasas 88) which apparently implies that everything except God perishes. The author explains that scholars have specified (takhsis) the generality of this verse, i.e., they limited its comprehensive scope so that it does not include things like the spirit, the tailbone, the Preserved Tablet, Paradise, Hell, etc. He defines specification as restricting the general to some of its individuals, and defines the general (al-'amm) as an expression that comprehensively includes everything qualified for it without enumeration (ghayr hasr). He then says that the poet (al-Laqqani) followed the response of a group including Ibn 'Abbas. Finally, he mentions the view of later verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun) that there is no exception or specification needed; rather, the meaning of 'perishing' in the verse is 'liable to perish' or 'possible to perish' due to its contingency and need, which is also the meaning of 'vanishing' (fanin). This view avoids the need for specification because the verse does not assert actual annihilation of everything, but rather its possibility.

Key Terms
تخصيص
عموم
عام
هالك
فان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'Everything is perishing' must be taken literally without any specification or reinterpretation, implying that nothing survives.
Correction: Scholars provide two valid approaches: either specify the verse to exclude certain entities, or reinterpret 'perishing' as 'liable to perish' due to contingency, which does not assert actual annihilation.

Checkpoint
What is the definition of 'general' (العام) according to this passage?
A) A word that includes a fixed number of individuals.
B) An expression that comprehensively includes everything qualified for it without enumeration.
C) A word that applies to all individuals without exception.
D) A word that is ambiguous and needs specification.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Everything is perishing' is interpreted by scholars either as a general statement specified by other texts, or as a statement about the inherent possibility of perishing, not actual annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite or hear the verse 'كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه', do you automatically assume you understand its full meaning? How does this lesson's demonstration of two scholarly interpretations challenge the confidence you place in your own initial understanding of Quranic verses? What will you do differently the next time you encounter a verse that seems absolute?
?
Are you willing to submit your interpretation to the authority of scholars who have spent their lives studying the Quran, even if their explanation contradicts your first impression? This passage shows that even a clear-seeming verse can be specified or reinterpreted. Is there an area in your faith where you resist scholarly guidance? Will you actively seek out such guidance this week?
?
The later scholars taught that 'everything perishes' means everything is inherently possible of perishing, not that it will actually perish. If you truly believed that every created thing—including your body, your wealth, your relationships—is contingent and only exists by God's will, how would your attachment to them change? What is one worldly thing you are clinging to that you need to release in light of this contingency?

Command to Refrain from Speculating on the Soul's Reality
Al-Amidi instructs against investigating the soul's essence, citing lack of revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic scholars prohibit independent rational investigation into the essence of the soul and how the correct stance is to rely solely on what has been revealed.

Core Idea
The soul's true nature is a divine secret, not to be probed beyond revelation.

In this lesson, we encounter a critical methodological principle: when the Lawgiver does not provide a detailed explanation of something, it is not our place to speculate. Al-Amidi, commenting on the poem, instructs believers not to delve into the reality of the soul because no text (nass) has come regarding its essence. Instead, they are to accept the hadith reported by Imam Malik that the soul is like a form within the body. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this prohibition and the etiquette required towards divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read its literal translation. Let the author's words set the tone.
Notice the poem's imperative voice: 'Do not delve.'
2
Identify the two groups and the chosen method
The commentary divides people into two groups: those who refrained and those who did not. Identify why the first group is considered the chosen approach.
The chosen method is to remain silent about the soul's essence.
3
Understand the reason for prohibition
The passage states that speculating is contrary to etiquette with the Lawgiver, as He did not explain the soul's reality even to the Prophet. What has come is only the hadith from Malik.
This reason is the core of the lesson: proper adab with revelation.

ولا نَخُضْ فِي الرُّوحِ إِذْ مَا وَرَدَا نَضٌ عَنِ الشَّارِعِ لَكِنْ وُجِدَا لِمَالك هِي صُورَةٌ كَالْجَسَدِ فَحَسْبُكَ النَّصُّ بِهَذَا السَّنَدِ. ولمَّا اختلفَ النَّاسُ في الرُّوحِ أيضًا على فرقتين: فرقة أمسكت عن الكلام فيها ؛ لأنَّها سِرّ مِن أسراره تعالى، لم يؤتِ علمه البشر، وكانت هذه الطَّريقة هى المختارة ؛ صَدَّرَ النَّاظِمُ جَازما بها فقال: (وَلَا نَخُضْن) نحنُ معاشِرَ جمهور المُحققين (في) بيان حقيقة (الرُّوحِ) بجنسِ وفَصلٍ مُمَيِّزَيْنِ لها ؛ لتعذر الوقوفِ عليهما ؛ لعدم ورود السمع بهما ، ولا يُتلقيان إلا منه . وأشار إلى علة النهي عن الخوض فيها على هذه الطريقة ، بأنَّه خِلافُ الأدب مع الشَّارع حيثُ لم يُبيِّنها لنبيه .. بقوله: (إِذْ مَا وَرَدَا)، أي: الشارع لم يرد نص في حقيقتها، والوارد هو الحديث: «الروح صورة كالجسد»، وهذا أخرجه مالك بسنده. فحسبك النص بهذا السند، أي: لا تحتاج إلى الخوض في حقيقتها وراء ذلك. ولهذه العلة تقتضي=
And do not delve into the soul, since no revelation came from the Lawgiver, but it is found that for Malik, it is a form like the body; so the text suffices you with this chain. And when people also differed regarding the soul into two groups: a group refrained from speaking about it because it is a secret of His secrets, whose knowledge was not given to humanity, and this method was the chosen one. So the author firmly prefaced it, saying: 'And we do not delve' – we, the community of the majority of verifiers – into clarifying the reality of the soul with a genus and differentiating differentia, because it is difficult to ascertain them due to the lack of transmitted revelation about them, and they can only be received from it. And he indicated the reason for the prohibition of delving into it in this manner: it is contrary to etiquette with the Lawgiver, as He did not explain it to His Prophet. His saying 'since no revelation came' means the Lawgiver did not bring a text concerning its reality, and what has come is the hadith: 'The soul is a form like the body,' and this was narrated by Malik with his chain. So the text suffices you with this chain, i.e., you do not need to delve into its reality beyond that. And this reason requires that...
Source pages p. 491

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the proper approach to the reality of the soul, based on the poem's instruction to refrain from speculation. The author first states the poem: 'Do not delve into the soul, since no revelation came from the Lawgiver, but it is found that for Malik, it is a form like the body; so the text suffices with this chain.' The commentary then explains that people differed on this issue into two groups: one group that refrained from speaking about it because it is a divine secret, and this is the chosen method. The author states that the group of verifiers (muhaqqiqun) takes this position: they do not attempt to define the soul by genus and differentia because no transmitted knowledge (naql) about those comes from revelation, and such definitions can only be received from revelation. He then indicates the reason for the prohibition: it is a breach of etiquette with the Lawgiver (shāriʿ) because He did not explain the soul's reality to the Prophet. What has come is only the hadith narrated by Malik that the soul is a form like the body. Therefore, that text suffices, and one should not go beyond it. The final sentence, though cut off, suggests that this reason necessitates further implications.

Key Terms
روح (rūḥ)
حقيقة (ḥaqīqah)
شَارِع (shāriʿ)
نص (naṣṣ)
سند (sanad)
صورة (ṣūrah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that rational investigation of the soul's essence is permissible and even praiseworthy.
Correction: The passage shows that such investigation is forbidden because it lacks textual basis and is disrespectful to the Lawgiver, who did not reveal the soul's essence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why should we not delve into the reality of the soul?
A) Because it is impossible to know anything about it.
B) Because no revelation came explaining its essence, and doing so would be improper etiquette toward the Lawgiver.
C) Because only prophets can know about it.
D) Because it is a material object that can be studied by science.

Key Takeaway
The passage teaches that when revelation is silent on a matter, the proper response is to refrain from speculation and accept what has been transmitted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there an area of faith or existence you have been trying to understand beyond what Allah has revealed? What does this lesson reveal about your adab with your Creator? Resolve to stop and simply accept His boundaries.
?
The soul is a secret of Allah's secrets. In your daily life, do you treat the unseen matters with sacred reverence, or do you let curiosity lead you to vain speculation? Before Allah, commit to guarding your tongue and heart from all that He has not disclosed.
?
When faced with a matter on which revelation is silent, do you humbly wait, or do you rush to fill the gap with reason? Think of one concrete situation where you can practice this restraint starting today.

Unseen Matters
