How Angels Question Many Deceased at Once
Text explains how two angels can question many deceased at once.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the two questioning angels can simultaneously address many deceased across different places, according to the explanations of al-Qurtubi and al-Suyuti.

Core Idea
Allah's power enables angels to address all deceased at once, making each feel uniquely addressed.

This lesson addresses a natural concern: if only two angels are assigned to question the dead, how can they handle countless people dying at the same time around the world? The scholars al-Qurtubi and al-Suyuti provide complementary explanations rooted in Allah’s absolute power. Let’s see how they resolve this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is dense but clear.
2
Understand al-Qurtubi's explanation
Al-Qurtubi explains that Allah magnifies the angels' capacity so they can address all the deceased with a single address, yet each deceased perceives the address as if it were directed solely to them. Allah also prevents them from hearing each other's responses.
3
Consider al-Suyuti's alternative
Al-Suyuti offers a different possibility: there may be multiple pairs of angels, not just one, to handle the multitude of deceased simultaneously.
This avoids the need for a single pair to address everyone at once.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Both explanations emphasize Allah's omnipotence over time, space, and individual perception. Reflect on how this reinforces the belief in divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا مات جماعةٌ في وقتٍ واحدٍ بأقَالِيمَ مُختلِفةٍ، جازَ أَنْ يُعظُمَ الله جُنَّتَهُما ويُخاطبان الخلقَ الكثير في الجهة الواحدة في المَرَّة الواحدة مُخاطبةً واحدةً بحيثُ يُخيَّلُ لِكُلِّ واحدٍ مِن المُخاطَبين أنَّه المُخاطَبُ دونَ مَن سِواه، ويمنعه الله تعالى من سماع جواب بقيَّة الموتى ، قاله القُرطبي . قال الحافظ السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى: ويحتمل تعدد الملائكة
And if a group dies at one time in different regions, it is possible that Allah magnifies their stature and they address the many creations in one direction at one time with a single address such that it appears to each of the addressees that he is the one being addressed excluding others, and Allah prevents him from hearing the answers of the rest of the dead. Al-Qurtubi said this. Al-Hafiz al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him, said: It is also possible that the angels are multiple.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage addresses a potential objection: how can only two angels (Munkar and Nakir) question countless people who die at the same time across different regions? The answer is given by al-Qurtubi: Allah, by His power, enables the angels to address all of them simultaneously in a single act that makes each deceased feel as if he is the sole addressee. The angels' words are heard by each individually, and simultaneously Allah prevents each deceased from hearing the answers of the others, preserving privacy. This is a manifestation of Allah's omnipotence, as He is not limited by time or space. The passage then notes an alternative view from al-Suyuti: it is possible that there are multiple pairs of angels, not just one pair, to handle the multitude. This avoids the difficulty of a single pair addressing everyone at once, though the first explanation already resolves it through divine power.

Key Terms
تعدد الملكين
الجهة الواحدة
تخيل الخطاب
القرطبي
السيوطي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think if many die at once, the angels cannot question them all due to spatial or temporal limitations.
Correction: Allah's power overcomes such limitations, either by enabling a single angelic pair to address everyone simultaneously with individual perception, or by providing multiple pairs of angels.

Checkpoint
How do the two angels question many who die simultaneously in different places according to al-Qurtubi?
A) They travel instantly between locations.
B) They address them all at once in a way that each feels uniquely addressed.
C) They only question one at a time, and others wait.
D) They send other angels to help.

Key Takeaway
Allah's omnipotence ensures that every deceased person is individually questioned by the angels, regardless of time or place.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that at the moment of your death, you will be individually questioned by angels, and that Allah will prevent you from hearing the answers of others, how does that change the way you view your personal accountability to Allah right now? What one sin will you repent from today because you know you cannot hide it in the grave?
?
The angels' ability to address many at once shows Allah's power over time and space. In what area of your life are you still acting as if Allah is limited by your circumstances? What practical step can you take to trust His power more?
?
Al-Qurtubi's explanation emphasizes that each deceased feels uniquely addressed. If you truly believed that you are personally and individually being observed by Allah at all times, what one behavior would you change starting today?

The Reality of Questioning in the Grave
Defines the reality of grave questioning: soul return, sense completion, and angelic role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the questioning in the grave is a real event involving the return of the entire soul and the completion of senses for the deceased to respond.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is real and sensory; the dead are fully revived for it.

This passage begins the discussion of the samiyyat by affirming the reality of the grave questioning. The author establishes that Allah returns the entire soul to the body and completes the senses so that the deceased can understand and answer. This counters any notion that the questioning is merely symbolic or spiritual.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall flow. Notice the sequential steps: soul return, sense completion, then questioning.
The passage is a continuous argument; let the author's logic unfold.
2
Identify the main claim
The author states that Allah returns the soul to the dead entirely (جميعه) – this is the position of the majority. Understand why this is important for the reality of the questioning.
This is a key doctrinal point against those who deny physical resurrection in the grave.
3
Understand the role of senses
Allah completes the senses so that the dead can hear, understand, and respond. Ask: Why is this necessary for the questioning?
The questioning is not just a spiritual experience; it involves real perception and response.
4
Reflect on the angels
The passage mentions the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) or one of them. Note that the author leaves room for variation in how many angels question.
This prepares for later details about simultaneous questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات • ، تعالى الرُّوحَ إلى الميت جميعه كما ذهب إليه الجمهور، وهو ظَاهِرُ الأحاديثِ، وتُكمَّلُ حَواسه، فَيَرُدُّ الله إليه ما يتوقف عليه فهم الخطاب، ويتأتى معه رَدُّ الجواب من الحواس والعقل والعلم، حتّى يسأله الملكان أو أحدهما، ويأخذ الله بأبصار الخَلائِق وأسماعهم، إلَّا مَن شاء الله عن حياة الميّت وما هو فيه عينًا وسماعاً، يَترفّقان بالمؤمن، وينتهران المُنافق والكافر، ويَسألان كُلّ أحدٍ بلسانه، ولو تمزقت أعضاؤه، أو أكلته السباع في أجوافها؛ إذ لا يَبعُد أن يَخلُقَ الله الحياة فيها، وأحوال المسؤولينَ مُختلفةٌ، فمنهم من يسأله الملكان جميعًا، ومنهم من يسأله أحدهما. وإذا مات جماعةٌ في وقتٍ واحدٍ بأقَالِيمَ مُختلِفةٍ، جازَ أَنْ يُعظُمَ الله جُنَّتَهُما ويُخاطبان الخلقَ الكثير في الجهة الواحدة في المَرَّة الواحدة مُخاطبةً واحدةً بحيثُ يُخيَّلُ لِكُلِّ واحدٍ مِن المُخاطَبين أنَّه المُخاطَبُ دونَ مَن سِواه، ويمنعه الله تعالى من سماع جواب بقيَّة الموتى، قاله القُرطبي. قال الحافظ السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى: ويحتمل تعدد الملائكة المُعدَّة لذلك، كما في الحفظة ونحوهم. قال: ثُمَّ رأيتُ الحَلِيمي ذهب إليه، فقال في منهاجه: والذي يشبه أنْ يكونَ ملائكةُ السُّؤالِ جماعة كثيرة يُسمّى بعضهم منكرًا وبعضهم نَكيرًا، فيُبعث إلى كُلِّ مَيّت اثنان منهم، والله أعلم. قال القُرطبي: اختلفت الأحاديثُ في كيفية السؤال والجواب، وذلك بحسب الأشخاص؛ فمنهم مَن يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم من يسأل عن كلها، انتهى.
The section of matters heard (samiyyat): He returns the soul to the dead person entirely, as the majority (jumhūr) held, and that is apparent from the hadiths. And his senses are completed, so Allah returns to him what is necessary for understanding the address, and with that, the response from the senses, intellect, and knowledge is possible, until the two angels or one of them question him. And Allah takes away the sight and hearing of creatures except whom Allah wills from the life of the dead and what he is in, sight and hearing. They are gentle with the believer and harsh with the hypocrite and disbeliever, and they question everyone in his own tongue, even if his limbs are torn apart or wild beasts have eaten him in their bellies, for it is not far that Allah creates life in them. And the conditions of those questioned vary: some are questioned by both angels, some by one of them. And if a group dies at the same time in different regions, it is permissible for Allah to enlarge their stature and for them to address many people in the same direction at the same time with one address such that each of those addressed imagines that he is the addressee to the exclusion of others, and Allah prevents him from hearing the answer of the rest of the dead. Al-Qurtubi said this. Al-Hafiz al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And it is possible that the angels are numerous for that purpose, as in the case of the guardian angels (ḥafazha) and the like. He said: Then I saw al-Ḥalīmī holding that view, so he said in his Minhāj: And what is likely is that the angels of questioning are a large group, some called Munkar and some Nakīr, and two of them are sent to every dead person. And Allah knows best. Al-Qurtubi said: The hadiths differ regarding the manner of questioning and answering, and that is according to the persons: some are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them. End.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is about the reality and details of the questioning in the grave, which is part of the samiyyat (matters known through revelation). The author first states the return of the entire soul to the dead body, as held by the majority, which is evident from hadith. He then explains that the senses are completed so that the dead person can understand the questioning and respond. The two angels (Munkar and Nakir) or one of them conduct the questioning. Allah blocks the senses of other creatures from perceiving the state of the dead. The angels are gentle with the believer and stern with the hypocrite. They question each person in his own language. Even if the body is destroyed, Allah can create life in it. Next, the author addresses the scenario of many people dying simultaneously in different places: it is possible for the angels to address all of them at once in a way that each feels individually addressed. Al-Qurtubi is cited for this. Then al-Suyuti suggests the possibility of multiple angels for questioning, citing al-Halimi who said that the angels of questioning are many, with some called Munkar and some Nakir, and two are sent to each dead person. Finally, al-Qurtubi notes that hadiths vary regarding the content of the questioning: some are asked about partial beliefs, others about all. This passage defends the doctrine that the grave questioning is real and that Allah's power encompasses all possibilities, including addressing many at once.

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
منكر ونكير
الرجوع إلى الميت
السمعيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The questioning in the grave is merely symbolic or happens only spiritually without the soul returning to the body.
Correction: The author affirms that the entire soul returns and senses are completed, making the questioning a real, physical event.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ruling on the return of the soul for the grave questioning?
A) Only a part of the soul returns.
B) The entire soul returns, as held by the majority.
C) The soul does not return; only the senses are created anew.
D) It is not known whether the soul returns.

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a real, physical event: the entire soul returns, senses are completed, and the angels question each person individually.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that after death you will be questioned in your own tongue by angels who know your every secret, what is the one thing you fear most about that moment? What are you doing today to prepare for that answer?
?
The passage says the angels are gentle with the believer and harsh with the hypocrite. If your heart were laid bare at that moment, which treatment would you deserve? What must change starting now?
?
You will be questioned even if your body is torn apart—nothing escapes. Does this reality change how you view your actions today? What specific sin will you repent from right now because you know you cannot hide from that questioning?

Details of the Angels and Simultaneous Questioning
Explains how angels question multiple dead simultaneously and the varying content of the questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah enables the angels to question many dead simultaneously and the varying content of the questioning based on hadith.

Core Idea
Allah empowers the angels to question multiple dead at once, each feeling individually addressed.

The passage continues with deeper details about the angels of the grave. It addresses a potential objection: how can the same two angels question many people dying at the same time in different places? The author explains that Allah can enlarge the angels and enable them to address all simultaneously. He also cites scholars on the possibility of a multitude of angels, and notes that the content of the questioning varies per person.

Guided Path
1
Focus on the simultaneous questioning
The passage states that if many die at the same time in different regions, Allah can make the angels address them all at once. Each person thinks he is the sole addressee.
This highlights Allah's absolute power over creation.
2
Explore the views of al-Qurtubi and al-Suyuti
Al-Qurtubi originally mentioned the simultaneous address; al-Suyuti suggests that there may be many angels, not just two named Munkar and Nakir.
Al-Halimi also held that the angels of questioning are a large group, with two sent to each dead person.
3
Understand the varying content
The passage ends with al-Qurtubi noting that hadiths differ: some are asked about all beliefs, others only about some.
This shows flexibility in the questioning based on the person's state.

5 min
The Reality of the Grave Questioning and Its Angels
Quotes al-Halimi and al-Qurtubi on the modality of grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the grave questioning, including the angels Munkar and Nakir, and how the modality of questioning varies according to the person's state.

Core Idea
The grave questioning is a real event with angels and variable questions based on one's beliefs.

This lesson explores the sam'iyy topic of the grave questioning. The passage draws on al-Halimi and al-Qurtubi to explain the identity of the questioning angels and why the modality of questions differs among people.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then refer to the English translation. Notice how the text transitions from a general statement to specific quotes from scholars.
2
Identify the key scholars quoted
The passage quotes al-Halimi and al-Qurtubi. Identify what each contributes: al-Halimi discusses the angels, al-Qurtubi addresses variability.
Both are authoritative Sunni scholars.
3
Understand the angels' role
Al-Halimi describes the angels as a large group with names Munkar and Nakir, and that two are sent to every deceased. Note that this is based on likeliness, not certainty.
The phrase 'والله أعلم' indicates scholarly humility.
4
Grasp the variability of questioning
Al-Qurtubi explains that hadiths differ because the questioning varies per person—some are asked about all beliefs, others only some. This shows divine wisdom.
This variability is in modality, not in the fact of questioning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
سؤال القبر ونعيمه وعذابه
المُعدَّة لذلك، كما في الحفظة ونحوهم. قال: ثُمَّ رأيتُ الحَلِيمي ذهب إليه، فقال في منهاجه : والذي يشبه أنْ يكونَ ملائكةُ السُّؤالِ جماعة كثيرة يُسمّى بعضهم منكرًا وبعضهم نَكيرًا ، فيُبعث إلى كُلِّ مَيّت اثنان منهم ، والله أعلم (۱) قال القُرطبي : اختلفت الأحاديثُ في كيفية السؤال والجواب، وذلك بحسب الأشخاص ؛ فمنهم مَن يُسأل عن بعض اعتقاداته، ومنهم من يسأل عن كلها ، انتهى .
وعن ابن عباس في قوله تعالى: يُثَبِّتُ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا بِالْقَوْلِ الثَّابِتِ [إبراهيم: (۲۷] ، قال : الشَّهادة ، يُسألونَ عنها في قبورهم بعد موتهم ، قيل لعكرمة ما هو ؟ قال : يُسألون عن الإيمان بمحمد الله ، وأمر التوحيد ، فيجيب بما يوافقُ مَا ماتَ عليه من إيمانٍ أو كفر أو شَكٍّ ، وهذا السؤال خاص بهذه الأمة. وقيل: وكلُّ نبي مع أمته كذلك.
The section on sam'iyyat (سمعيات). The questioning of the grave, its bliss and its punishment. [The angels] prepared for that, as in the keepers and the like. He said: Then I saw al-Halimi inclined to it, and he said in his Manhaj: 'What is likely is that the angels of questioning are a large group, some called Munkar and some Nakir, and two of them are sent to every deceased, and Allah knows best.' (1) Al-Qurtubi said: 'The hadiths differ concerning the modality of the question and answer, and that is according to persons; some are asked about some of their beliefs, and some are asked about all of them.' End. And from Ibn Abbas concerning the saying of Allah, the Exalted: 'Allah confirms those who believe with the firm word' [Ibrahim: 27]. He said: 'The testimony; they are asked about it in their graves after their death.' It was said to Ikrimah: 'What is it?' He said: 'They are asked about faith in Muhammad, the Messenger of Allah, and the matter of tawhid (توحيد), and they answer according to what they died upon of faith or disbelief or doubt.' And this questioning is specific to this Ummah. And it is said: And every prophet with his Ummah is likewise.
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of the grave questioning (su'al al-qabr) as a sam'iyy issue known from revelation. It begins by affirming that angels are prepared for this task, like the recording angels (hafazah). It then presents the view of al-Halimi that the questioning angels are a large group with specific names (Munkar and Nakir), and two are dispatched to every deceased person. Al-Qurtubi is then quoted to clarify that the hadiths vary regarding the modality of the question and answer, and that this variation is according to the person's state—some are questioned about a portion of their beliefs, others about all of them. The passage then cites the commentary of Ibn Abbas on Qur'an 14:27, explaining that 'the firm word' is the shahadah (testimony of faith), about which the deceased are asked. Ikrimah clarifies that they are asked about faith in Muhammad ﷺ and about tawhid. The answer matches what they died upon—faith, disbelief, or doubt. Finally, two views are noted: one that this questioning is specific to this Ummah, and another that every prophet's nation undergoes the same.

Key Terms
سؤال القبر
منكر ونكير
السؤال والجواب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The grave questioning is a physical test and the same for all people, or that the hadiths contradict each other.
Correction: The questioning is a spiritual reality known from revelation, and the hadiths differ because the modality varies according to the person's state, as al-Qurtubi explains.

Checkpoint

A) One
B) Two
C) Many
D) None

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a real event involving specific angels (Munkar and Nakir), and the questions vary according to each person's state of belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
How does the fact that the questions in the grave vary according to each person's individualized state change the way you think about preparing for your own death? What specific belief do you need to strengthen?

The Content of the Grave Questioning: Tawhid and Shahadah
Cites Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah on the qur'anic basis for grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the core of the grave questioning is about faith in Allah and His Messenger, as indicated by the verse from Ibrahim and the interpretations of Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah.

Core Idea
The grave question is about the shahadah, and the answer matches one's final state.

This lesson delves into the qur'anic basis for the grave questioning, focusing on the verse from Surah Ibrahim. Ibn Abbas interprets 'the firm word' as the testimony of faith, and Ikrimah expands on the content of the questioning, which centers on faith in Prophet Muhammad and tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Ibn Abbas and Ikrimah
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that this passage cites a Qur'anic verse and its interpretation by a Companion and a Tabi'i.
2
Understand the meaning of 'the firm word'
Ibn Abbas says 'the firm word' is the shahadah. This means the questioning is about affirming faith in Allah and His Messenger.
This directly connects the verse to the grave questioning.
3
Learn the content of the questioning
Ikrimah specifies that they are asked about faith in Muhammad (ﷺ) and the matter of tawhid. The answer is according to what they died upon.
4
Note the two views on scope
The passage ends with two opinions: one that this questioning is specific to the Ummah of Muhammad (ﷺ), and another that every prophet's nation is questioned similarly.
Both views are transmitted.

Commentary
This passage defines the reality of the grave questioning (su'al al-qabr) as a sam'iyy issue known from revelation. It begins by affirming that angels are prepared for this task, like the recording angels (hafazah). It then presents the view of al-Halimi that the questioning angels are a large group with specific names (Munkar and Nakir), and two are dispatched to every deceased person. Al-Qurtubi is then quoted to clarify that the hadiths vary regarding the modality of the question and answer, and that this variation is according to the person's state—some are questioned about a portion of their beliefs, others about all of them. The passage then cites the commentary of Ibn Abbas on Qur'an 14:27, explaining that 'the firm word' is the shahadah (testimony of faith), about which the deceased are asked. Ikrimah clarifies that they are asked about faith in Muhammad ﷺ and about tawhid. The answer matches what they died upon—faith, disbelief, or doubt. Finally, two views are noted: one that this questioning is specific to this Ummah, and another that every prophet's nation undergoes the same.

Exemptions from the Grave Questioning
Lists categories exempt from grave questioning with explanatory footnotes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which categories of people are exempt from the grave questioning according to transmitted evidence, and the rationale behind these exemptions.

Core Idea
Grave questioning is not universal; Allah exempts specific groups based on rank, deeds, and circumstances.

The author al-Laqani clarifies that the grave questioning is not for everyone. He lists several categories based on transmitted reports (athar) of exemption. These include prophets, the sincere, frontier guards, martyrs, those with specific recitation habits, those who die under certain conditions, and those with mental incapacity. Let's explore each category and the clarifications provided by al-Shanawani.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the English translation. Notice the list-like structure.
The passage is a continuous enumeration; the footnotes (numbers in brackets) are explained separately.
2
Understand the principle of exemption
The opening states that questioning is specific to those for whom no report of exemption exists. This sets the rule: exemption is known only by transmitted evidence.
3
Identify the first set of exempt categories
These include prophets (especially the Prophet Muhammad, about whom there should be no dispute), the siddiq (sincere believer, not only Abu Bakr), frontier guards (murābiṭūn), martyrs, and those who habitually recite Surat al-Mulk and Surat al-Sajdah every night.
Al-Shanawani explains that habit means regular performance from the time one learns about the virtue until death.
4
Identify the second set of exempt categories
These include: reciting Surat al-Ikhlas during the fatal illness, dying of stomach disease, dying on Friday night or Friday day (even if buried later), dying of plague (or during a plague while patiently expecting reward), the insane, the simpleton (ablah), and the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah).
The exemption for ahl al-fatrah applies only if the grave questioning is not specific to this Ummah.
5
Note the clarifications from al-Shanawani
Al-Shanawani's footnotes explain key terms: siddiq is general, mulāzama means regular performance, the time boundaries for Friday, and the definition of ablah as someone naive in worldly affairs.
These clarifications prevent misunderstandings, like limiting siddiq to Abu Bakr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والعموم في قول النَّاظم «سؤالنا مَخصوص بمَن وردَ الأثر بعدم سؤاله ، كالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، ولا ينبغي أن يكون سيّدهم الأعظمُ محل خلاف، وكالصِّدِّيقِ (۱) ، والمُرابطين ، والشَّهداء، ومُلازِم (۲) قراءة سورة تبارك ، المُلْك كلَّ ليلةٍ وسورة السجدة» فيما ذكره بعضهم، وكذا مَن قرأ في مرضه الذي مات فيه: ﴿قُلْ هُوَ اللهُ أَحَدٌ ﴾ [الإخلاص: ١] ، ومريض البطن، ومَيِّتِ ليلة الجمعة أو يومها(۳) ، كالميت بالطاعون أو في زمنه ولو بغيره صابرا محتسبا ، وكالمجنونِ والأَبْله (٤) وأهل الفترة .. إن قلنا بعدم اختصاصه بهذه الأمة. (۱) قوله: (وكالصديق) المراد به كل من صدق الله ورسوله، وأخلص لله ظاهرا وباطنا، لا خصوص أبي بكر فقط . الشنواني . (۲) قوله (و ملازم (قراءة أي من حين بلوغ الخبر ،له والمراد بالملازمة الإتيان بها في غالب الأوقات من حين بلوغ الخبر إلى انقضاء العمر، فلا يضر الترك مرة بعذر . الشنواني . (۳) قوله: (وميت ليلة الجمعة وتدخل ليلتها بزوال شمس يوم الخميس ، وينقضي يوم الجمعة بغروب شمسه، ولو لم يدفن إلا يوم السبت الشنواني . (٤) قوله : (الأبله) المراد به المغفل في أمر دنياه، وإن كان له عقل لكن لا يصل لحد التدبير . الشنواني
And the generality in the saying of the author: 'Our questioning is specific to those for whom the report has come of no questioning, such as the prophets, peace be upon them; and their greatest master should not be a subject of disagreement; and like the siddiq (1), and the murābiṭūn (those stationed on frontiers), and the martyrs, and the one who makes a habit (2) of reciting Surat Tabarak (al-Mulk) every night and Surat al-Sajdah' according to what some have mentioned; and likewise the one who recites in his illness from which he dies: 'Say: He is Allah, the One' [al-Ikhlas: 1], and the one with a stomach disease, and the one who dies on the night of Friday or its day (3), like the one who dies of plague or in its time even if by another cause, patient and expecting reward; and like the insane and the simpleton (4) and the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) ... if we say that it is not specific to this Ummah. (1) His saying: 'and like the siddiq' – by it is meant everyone who sincerely believes Allah and His Messenger and is sincere to Allah outwardly and inwardly, not only Abu Bakr. Al-Shanawani. (2) His saying: 'and the one who makes a habit of reciting' – i.e. from the time the report reaches him; what is meant by habit is performing it most of the time from the time the report reaches him until the end of life, and missing once due to an excuse does not harm. Al-Shanawani. (3) His saying: 'the one who dies on the night of Friday' – its night enters with the decline of the sun of Thursday, and Friday ends with the setting of its sun, even if he is not buried until Saturday. Al-Shanawani. (4) His saying: 'the simpleton' – by it is meant the one who is heedless in his worldly affairs, even if he has intellect but it does not reach the level of management. Al-Shanawani.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of those exempt from the grave questioning, based on transmitted reports (athar). The author (al-Laqani in his poem) states that the questioning is specific to those for whom there is no evidence of exemption. The categories listed include: the prophets (with emphasis that the Prophet ﷺ should not be disputed), the siddiq (explained by al-Shanawani as any sincere believer, not only Abu Bakr), the murābiṭūn (those guarding frontiers), the martyrs (shuhadā'), those who habitually recite Surat al-Mulk and Surat al-Sajdah every night, those who recite al-Ikhlas in their fatal illness, those who die of stomach disease, those who die on Friday night or Friday day (with al-Shanawani defining the time boundaries), those who die of plague or in a plague time patiently expecting reward, the insane, the simpleton (ablah), and the people of the interval (ahl al-fatrah) – those who lived in a period without a prophet. The passage ends with a condition that this exemption applies if we hold that the questioning is not specific to this Ummah. The footnotes by al-Shanawani clarify the meanings: siddiq is general; mulāzama (habit) means regular performance from the time one learns of the virtue; Friday night and day are astronomically defined; and ablah is not a complete idiot but someone naive in worldly matters.

Correction: Al-Shanawani explains that siddiq refers to anyone who sincerely believes Allah and His Messenger and is sincere outwardly and inwardly.

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is not for everyone; many are exempt due to their high rank, specific deeds, or circumstances as revealed in transmitted reports.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Firm Word: Quranic Basis for Grave Questioning
Ibn Abbas interprets the firm word verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic basis for the questioning in the grave and what the 'firm word' refers to according to Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
The firm word is the testimony of faith, the basis for grave questioning.

This lesson examines a key Quranic verse that establishes the reality of the grave questioning. Ibn Abbas, the cousin of the Prophet ﷺ, provides a direct interpretation that ties the verse to the shahada. Understanding this connection is essential for appreciating the sam‘iyyāt (matters known through revelation).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the flow from verse citation to interpretation.
2
Identify Ibn Abbas's interpretation
Focus on what Ibn Abbas says the 'firm word' is. He says it is the testimony (shahada). Understand that this testimony is the content of the grave questioning.
The questioning is about belief in Muhammad and tawhid.
3
Understand the scope of the questioning
The passage states this questioning is specific to this ummah, though some say every prophet's ummah is similarly questioned. Reflect on the importance of this for our faith.
This connects to the broader doctrine of the barzakh.

Exemptions from Grave Questioning
Enumerating categories exempted from grave questioning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various categories of people who are exempt from the questioning in the grave according to transmitted reports in the Sunni tradition.

Core Idea
Many believers are exempt from grave questioning by divine mercy and specific merit.

The poet al-Laqqani states that grave questioning is not universal; certain individuals are exempt based on prophetic reports. This passage from the commentary lists these exemptions, highlighting special ranks and acts that remove the trial of the grave. The teacher explains that even among Muslims, many are spared this ordeal.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of exemption
The passage begins by noting that the poet's wording 'our questioning' implies not everyone is questioned. Read the opening to grasp that exemptions are based on transmitted reports.
The principle: questioning is only for those not specifically exempted.
2
Identify the first group: prophets
Prophets are exempt, especially Prophet Muhammad. The commentator stresses that there should be no disagreement about him.
This is the highest exemption.
3
Note other meritorious categories
The siddiq (truthful one), murābiṭūn (frontier guards), martyrs, and those who regularly recite Surah al-Mulk and Surah al-Sajdah are exempt. Recognize their special status.
These are based on specific hadiths.
4
Consider additional exemptions
Further exemptions include reciting Surah al-Ikhlas in final illness, stomach illness, death on Friday or its night, death from plague with patience, insane, simpleton, and people of the fatrah (interval between prophets).
This shows the breadth of divine mercy.

Who is questioned in his grave and who is not questioned? And the general import in the statement of the poet: 'Our questioning is exclusive to those for whom a report has come establishing their not being questioned, such as the prophets – peace and blessings be upon them – and it is not fitting that their greatest master (the Prophet Muhammad) be a subject of disagreement, and like the siddīq (truthful one) (1), and the murābiṭūn (those stationed on frontiers), and the martyrs, and the one who is constant (2) in reciting Surah Tabārak (i.e., al-Mulk) every night and Surah al-Sajdah' according to what some have mentioned. Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage enumerates categories of people who are not questioned in the grave according to transmitted reports. It begins with the general principle from the poet (al-Laqqani) that questioning is only for those for whom there is no report of exemption. Then it lists the exempted: prophets (with emphasis that the Prophet Muhammad is unquestionably included), the siddīq (truthful one, explained in footnote as anyone who sincerely believes in Allah and His Messenger), the murābiṭūn (those guarding frontiers), martyrs, and those who regularly recite Surah al-Mulk and Surah al-Sajdah every night. Additional exemptions mentioned by some include whoever recites surah al-Ikhlas in their final illness, those with stomach illness, those who die on Friday night or day, those who die from plague or during plague time patiently, the insane, the simpleton, and the people of the fatrah (interval between prophets) if we hold that the questioning is not specific to this ummah.

أهل الفترة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Muslims will be questioned in the grave; no one is exempt.
Correction: Many categories of believers are exempt, including prophets, martyrs, and those with specific meritorious acts or conditions.

Checkpoint

A) Prophets
B) Martyrs
C) Hypocrites
D) Those who recite Surah al-Mulk nightly

Key Takeaway
Grave questioning is not universal; many believers are spared through prophetic privilege, martyrdom, specific devotions, or divine mercy in special circumstances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Children and Angels Not Questioned in the Grave
Affirming questioning is for accountable beings only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why most scholars hold that questioning in the grave applies only to those who are legally accountable (mukallaf) and not to children or angels.

Core Idea
Grave questioning is only for accountable beings, not children or angels.

After establishing the realities of the grave and its questioning, the author turns to a subtle point: who exactly is questioned? This passage addresses the status of children and angels, clarifying that the sound position is to refrain from asserting that children are questioned, and to hold that angels are not questioned at all. The key principle is that questioning is tied to legal accountability (taklif).

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once to get its rhythm. Notice the key terms: المكلف, الوقف, الأطفال, الملائكة.
The passage begins with a general question and then states the correct stance.
2
Understand the two rulings
Identify that the passage makes two separate claims: (1) about children – it is safer to withhold a definite answer, but the apparent view is that they are not questioned; (2) about angels – the apparent view is that they are not questioned at all.
The reason given: questioning is for those who are buried (i.e., humans).
3
Connect to the principle of taklif
Realise that the underlying principle is legal accountability (taklif). Only those who have reached the age of accountability and have received the message are subject to questioning.
This connects to the broader kalam discussion of who is tested and judged.
4
Reflect on the adverb 'apparent' (الظاهر)
The author uses الظاهر twice, indicating that these are the prevailing scholarly views, not absolute certainties. This shows scholarly caution.

Commentary
This passage states the correct stance on the grave questioning of children and angels. The footnote explains that angels do not die except at the first trumpet blast.

The Questioning of Jinn and the Meaning of Fitna in the Grave
Explains jinn are questioned and defines the grave fitna as a test with three perspectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that jinn are questioned in the grave and what the fitna (trial) means, including its three perspectives and the divine wisdom behind it.

Core Idea
The grave's fitna reveals what the heart hides—jinn and humans alike are tested.

In this lesson, we examine a passage from a classical Kalam text that addresses two related matters: the inclusion of jinn in the grave questioning and the nature of that questioning as a fitna. The author relies on the authority of Imam Jalāl al-Suyūṭī and proceeds to unpack the meaning of fitna as a test that involves the deceased, the living, and the angels. This helps us understand the purpose of such tests despite Allah's complete knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once through. Notice the structure: first jinn, then definition of fitna, then three perspectives, then wisdom.
The text ends with 'ليباهي' which is cut off; the meaning is completed by context.
2
Understand the inclusion of jinn
The author asserts jinn are questioned because they are legally responsible (mukallaf) and the general texts apply to all responsible beings.
This is a matter of samiyyat (unseen matters) accepted from revelation.
3
Analyze the definition of fitna
Fitna is defined as testing and examining (al-ikhtibār wa al-imtiḥān). Note the three perspectives: the deceased, us (the living), and the angels.
The test is not for Allah's knowledge but to manifest hidden deeds.
4
Ponder the wisdom
The wisdom is to manifest what was concealed so that Allah may boast (or disgrace) to the angels.
The word 'ليباهي' indicates divine boasting in a manner befitting His majesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا الجِنُّ .. فجزمَ الجَلالُ بسؤالهم؛ لتكليفهم وعموم، وهذا السؤال هو نفس الفتنة وهي: الاختبار والامتحان بالنظر إلى الميّت (۳) أو إلينا (٤) أو إلى الملائكة (٥) ، لإحاطة علمه تعالى بكلّ شيء؛ فحكمته إظهار ما كتمه العِباد في الدُّنيا من كفر أو إيمان أو طاعةٍ أو عصيان الله بهم الملائكة أو ليُفضَحُوا عندهم. ليباهي
As for the jinn – Jalāl asserted their questioning, because they are legally responsible and (the text is) general. And this questioning is itself the fitna (trial), which is: testing and examining with respect to the deceased (3) or to us (4) or to the angels (5), because His knowledge, exalted is He, encompasses everything. So His wisdom is to manifest what the servants concealed in the world of disbelief or faith or obedience or disobedience, to boast with them to the angels or to disgrace them before them.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage discusses the grave questioning of jinn and the nature of the fitna (trial). It begins by stating that Jalāl al-Suyūṭī definitively holds that jinn are questioned because they are mukallaf (legally responsible) and the general texts apply to them. The questioning itself is the fitna, which means testing and examining. This test has three perspectives: with respect to the deceased (whether he answers correctly), with respect to us (whether we believe in it), and with respect to the angels (whether they fulfil their duty). The wisdom behind it, despite Allah's omniscience, is to manifest what people concealed in this world—whether good or evil—so that Allah may boast about them to the angels or disgrace them before them.

Key Terms
الجن
الفتنة
الاختبار
الامتحان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The grave questioning is only for punishment.
Correction: It is also a test and a display of hidden deeds, as the passage defines fitna as testing and examination, not merely punishment.

Checkpoint

A) Punishment
B) A test and examination
C) A reward
D) An interrogation by angels

Key Takeaway
The grave fitna is a test of faith that applies to both humans and jinn, revealing their true state for divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe you are a believer, but your heart hides doubts and sins. When the grave's test exposes what you have concealed, will you be disgraced or boasted of? What secret disobedience are you nurturing right now that you know would shame you in that moment?
?
If Allah already knows your faith, why must it be displayed through the fitna? Are you living a faith that is only external, relying on 'knowing' while your inner state remains neglected? The grave test will strip away pretense. What will remain when your deeds are laid bare before the angels?
?
The jinn are also questioned—they too face accountability. Do you take the unseen realities of the grave as seriously as the visible world? Your actions today are not for show; they are being recorded for a trial that will manifest them. How would you change your life if you truly believed that the first question after death will expose the core of your faith?

The Reality of the Punishment of the Grave
Defines punishment of grave as barzakh punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the punishment of the grave is the barzakh punishment and applies to all deceased, whether buried or not.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave is not limited to graves—it is the barzakh punishment for all.

This passage clarifies a key Sunni belief about the afterlife: the punishment of the grave. Sanusi explains that it is not confined to physical interment but is a punishment of the barzakh, the intermediate state between death and resurrection. Understanding this distinction removes a common misunderstanding and affirms the universal scope of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note how Sanusi connects this topic to the previous discussion of questioning in the grave.
The passage is short but dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key definition
Find where Sanusi defines the punishment of the grave as the punishment of the barzakh. This is the central doctrinal point.
3
Understand the reason for its name
Read why it is called 'punishment of the grave' even though it applies to all. This addresses a common misconception.
It is called that because burial is the most common case.
4
Reflect on theological implications
Think about what this means for those who are not buried—crucified, drowned, eaten by animals. The punishment is real and not dependent on physical burial.
This affirms Allah's absolute power over the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ عَذَابُ القَبْرِ) عطف على سؤالنا» لمشاركته له في حكمه(٦) الآتي، يعني وممَّا يجب الإيمانُ به حَقِيَّةُ (٧) عذاب القبر، وهو عذاب البرزخ، أضيف إلى القبر لأنَّه الغالب (۸) ، وإلا فكل ميت أراد الله تعالى ناله ما أراده به قبر أو لم يُقبَر ، ولو صُلب أو غَرق في بحر ، أو أكلته

Otherwise, every deceased person whom Allah wills to punish, He inflicts upon him what He wills whether he is buried or not, even if he is crucified or drowns in the sea, or is eaten by...
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligation to believe in the reality of the punishment of the grave. It begins by noting that the phrase 'the punishment of the grave' is joined to the earlier discussion of questioning in the grave because it shares the same legal ruling (obligation to believe). The punishment of the grave is identified as the punishment of the barzakh (the intermediate state between death and resurrection). It is called 'punishment of the grave' because burial is the most common way the deceased are treated, but the punishment is not limited to those buried. Any deceased person—whether crucified, drowned, or eaten by beasts—may be punished by Allah as He wills. The footnote explains that the ruling is legal obligation (wājib shar‘ī).

Who Is Questioned in the Grave and the Nature of the Trial
Enumeration and explanation of who is questioned in the grave.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand which categories of beings are subject to the questioning in the grave according to the apparent view, and the purpose of this questioning as a divine trial.

Core Idea
The grave's questioning tests faith, but not all beings face it.

In this passage, the author clarifies a debated aspect of eschatology: who exactly is questioned by the angels in the grave. He discusses children, angels, and jinn, and explains that the questioning serves as a trial to manifest hidden truths.

Guided Path
1
Learn the ruling for children
Read the passage on children: the correct position is to refrain from definitively stating that they are questioned; the apparent view restricts questioning to those who are morally obligated (mukallaf).
This shows caution in theological rulings where clear evidence is lacking.
2
Learn the ruling for angels and jinn
Angels are not questioned because they are not buried. Jinn, however, are definitively questioned because they are obligated and general evidence applies.
The distinction is based on burial and moral obligation.
3
Understand the trial (fitna)
The questioning itself is a trial: it tests and examines the deceased, the living, or the angels. Its wisdom is to manifest what the servants concealed in this world, so that Allah may boast with them or they may be disgraced.
This connects the grave questioning to divine wisdom and accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَن يُسأَلُ في قَبْره ومَن لا يُسأَل
والحَقُّ : الوقفُ عن الجزم بسؤال الأطفال ، بل الظَّاهرُ ـ كما جزم به الجَلالُ السُّيوطِيُّ وغيره - : اختصاص السُّؤالِ بمن يكونُ مُكلَّفا ، كما أَنَّ الظَّاهِرَ عدم سؤالِ الملائكة ، لأنَّه لمن شأنه أنْ يُقبَر .

Who is questioned in his grave and who is not questioned. The correct view is to refrain from definitively stating the questioning of children, rather the apparent view, as decided by al-Jalal al-Suyuti and others, is that questioning is specific to those who are morally obligated, and likewise the apparent view is that angels are not questioned because they are not of the kind that are buried. To them is the evidence of questioning. As for the jinn, al-Jalal definitively stated that they are questioned because they are obligated and the general [evidence]. Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage defines who is subject to the questioning in the grave. It begins by stating the topic: who is questioned and who is not. Then it gives the correct position: one should refrain from definitively stating whether children are questioned; the apparent view, as al-Suyuti and others held, is that questioning is only for the morally obligated (mukallaf). Angels are not questioned because they are not buried. As for the jinn, al-Suyuti definitively stated they are questioned because they are obligated and the general evidence applies. The passage then explains the nature of the questioning: it is a trial (fitna) and an examination that relates to the deceased, to us (the living), or to the angels. Its wisdom is to manifest what people concealed in this world, whether disbelief, faith, obedience, or disobedience, so that Allah may show off to the angels or so that the deceased may be disgraced. The author thus establishes the scope and purpose of the grave questioning.

The Reality of Punishment of the Grave
The author defines the punishment of the grave, its locus, evidence, and rational permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality of punishment of the grave, its locus in body and soul, its scriptural evidence, and why it is rationally possible.

Core Idea
Punishment of the grave applies to all deceased, body and soul, not just those buried.

This lesson clarifies a foundational belief in Islamic eschatology: the punishment of the grave (ʿadhāb al-qabr). The author defines it as the punishment of the barzakh, explains that it affects both body and soul, and provides both rational and scriptural evidence. Read on to understand what every Muslim must believe about this intermediate state.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and scope
Begin by reading how the author defines punishment of the grave and notes that it applies to all deceased, not only the buried.
Notice the phrase 'أضيف إلى القبر لأنَّه الغالب'.
2
Identify the locus of punishment
Find where the text states the locus: body and soul together after the soul is returned.
The consensus of Ahl al-Ḥaqq is mentioned.
3
Note the categories of people
List who experiences this punishment: disbelievers, hypocrites, sinful believers, and all nations.
4
Examine the evidence
Read the Quranic verse (40:46) and the rational argument. Understand why it is obligatory to accept.
The passage concludes that Allah is powerful over all things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ثُمَّ عَذَابُ القَبْرِ) عطف على سؤالنا لمشاركته له في حكمه الآتي، يعني وممَّا يجب الإيمانُ به حَقِيَّةُ عذاب القبر، وهو عذاب البرزخ، أضيف إلى القبر لأنَّه الغالب ، وإلا فكل ميت أراد الله تعالى ناله ما أراده به قبر أو لم يُقبَر ، ولو صُلب أو غَرق في بحر ، أو أكلته الدَّوابُ ، أو حُرقَ حَتَّى صارَ رمادًا وذُرِيَ في الرّيح ، ومحله: البَدَن والرُّوح جميعاً ، باتّفاق أهل الحقِّ ، بعد إعادة الرُّوح إليه أو إلى جُزء مِنه إِنْ قلنا: إِنَّ المُعذَّب بعض الجسد ولا يمنعُ من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرّقت أجزاؤُه ، أو أكلته السباع أو حِيتَانُ البحر أو نحو ذلك ، ويكون للكافر والمنافق وعُصاة المؤمنين ، ولهذه الأُمَّة ،وغيرها ، ودليل وقوعه قوله تعالى: ﴿النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوًّا وَعَشِيَّا﴾ [غافر: ٤٦] ، ولا يمتنع عند العقل أنْ يُعيدَ الله الحياة في الجسد أو في جُزء منه ويعذِّبه ، وكلُّ ما لم يمنعه العقل ووَرَدَ بوقوعه الشَّرعُ .. وجبَ قبوله واعتقاده، والله يفعل ما يَشَاء مِن عِقابِ ونَعِيمٍ، ويَصْرِفُ أبصَارَنَا ويحجبها عن جميعه ؛ لأنَّه القادر على كُلّ ممكن.
Then (the punishment of the grave) is coordinated with 'our questioning' because it shares the same ruling to come, meaning: it is among the things that must be believed in—the reality of the punishment of the grave, and it is the punishment of the barzakh, attributed to the grave because it is the most common, otherwise every deceased person whom Allah intends to punish, He afflicts him with what He wills, whether buried or not, even if crucified, drowned in the sea, eaten by beasts, burned until ashes and scattered in the wind. Its locus is the body and the soul together, by consensus of the people of truth, after the soul is returned to it or to a part of it if we say that the punished is part of the body. And the fact that the dead body's parts have separated, or been eaten by predators or sea fish or the like does not prevent that. And it is for the disbeliever, the hypocrite, and the sinful believers, and for this ummah and others. The evidence of its occurrence is His statement: 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' (40:46). It is not rationally impossible for Allah to restore life to the body or a part of it and punish it. Everything that reason does not preclude and that revelation confirms as occurring must be accepted and believed. Allah does whatever He wills of punishment and bliss, and He averts our eyes and veils us from all of it because He is powerful over everything possible.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage defines the punishment of the grave (ʿadhāb al-qabr). It begins by noting that this topic is coordinated with the previous discussion of questioning because they share the same ruling: necessary belief. The punishment is identified as the punishment of the barzakh (intermediate state), called 'grave punishment' because burial is the most common case, but it applies to every deceased whom Allah wills to punish, regardless of whether they are buried, crucified, drowned, eaten, or cremated. The text then states its locus (maḥall): the body and soul together, by consensus of Ahl al-Ḥaqq, after the soul is returned to the body or a part of it. The fact that the body may have disintegrated or been consumed does not prevent this. The punishment is for the disbeliever, the hypocrite, and the sinful believer, and for this ummah and others. The proof from revelation is the verse 'The Fire, they are exposed to it morning and evening' (Ghāfir 40:46). Rationally, it is not impossible for Allah to restore life and punish. Whatever reason does not deny and revelation affirms must be accepted. The passage concludes that Allah is able to do all possible things, and He veils our sight from these punishments.

برزخ
بدن
روح
إعادة الروح
عقل
شرع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Punishment of the grave only occurs if one is buried in a grave.
Correction: The text explains that the punishment applies to every deceased person whom Allah wills to punish, regardless of burial, even if cremated or eaten.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is real, affects body and soul, and is a matter of necessary belief based on both reason and revelation.

?

?

Reality and Location of the Punishment of the Grave
Defines the reality and location of the punishment of the grave with evidence and rational justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the reality and locus of the punishment of the grave according to Ahl al-Sunnah, including its evidence and rational basis.

Core Idea
The punishment of the grave affects both body and soul, by divine power, after the soul is returned to the body.

This lesson unpacks the doctrine of the punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr), a core belief from the Sam'iyyat (audible matters) in Sunni theology. The passage affirms that punishment affects both body and soul after their reunion, addresses objections about bodily decay, and provides scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own statements come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise style and the use of technical terms.
2
Identify the locus of punishment
Locate the sentence stating the locus (mahall). Note that it is both body and soul together, and that the soul is returned to the body or a part thereof.
This directly refutes the idea that only the soul is punished.
3
Consider the objection of bodily disintegration
Find where the author addresses the possibility that the body has disintegrated or been eaten. Understand why this does not prevent punishment.
The key is God's power to return the soul to any part.
4
List the categories of people
Identify the three groups mentioned: disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful believers. Note that it applies to this ummah and others.
5
Understand the evidence and rational basis
Read the Quranic evidence (Ghafir 40:46) and the logical principle: if intellect does not preclude and revelation confirms, belief is obligatory.
This connects the doctrine to broader kalam methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات. الدَّوابُ ، أو حُرقَ حَتَّى صارَ رمادًا وذُرِيَ في الرّيح ، ومحله البَدَن والرُّوح جميعاً ، باتّفاق أهل الحق ، بعد إعادة الرُّوح إليه أو إلى جُزء مِنه إِنْ قلنا: إِنَّ المُعذَّب بعض الجسد ولا يمنعُ من ذلك كون الميت قد تفرّقت أجزاؤُه ، أو أكلته السباع أو حِيتَانُ البحر أو نحو ذلك ، ويكون للكافر والمنافق وعُصاة المؤمنين ، ولهذه الأُمَّة ،وغيرها ، ودليل وقوعه قوله تعالى: ﴿النَّارُ يُعْرَضُونَ عَلَيْهَا غُدُوًّا وَعَشِيَّا﴾ [غافر: ٤٦] ، ولا يمتنع عند العقل أنْ يُعيدَ الله الحياة في الجسد أو في جُزء منه ويعذِّبه ، وكلُّ ما لم يمنعه العقل ووَرَدَ بوقوعه الشَّرعُ .. وجبَ قبوله واعتقاده، والله يفعل ما يَشَاء مِن عِقابِ ونَعِيمٍ، ويَصْرِفُ أبصَارَنَا ويحجبها عن جميعه ؛ لأنَّه القادر على كُلّ ممكن.
Section on the Audible (Sam'iyyat). [If the deceased is] eaten by beasts, or burned until becoming ashes and scattered in the wind, its locus (mahall) is the body and the soul together, by agreement of the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq), after the soul is returned to it or to a part of it if we say that the punished one is some of the body. And it is not prevented by the fact that the dead may have had its parts scattered, or been eaten by predators or fish of the sea or the like. And it applies to the disbeliever, the hypocrite, and the sinful believers, and to this community (ummah) and others. The evidence of its occurrence is the saying of the Most High: {The Fire; they are exposed to it morning and evening} [Ghafir: 46]. And it is not impossible for the intellect that God should return life to the body or to a part of it and punish it. And everything that the intellect does not prevent and the Law (shar') has reported its occurrence, it is obligatory to accept and believe it. And God does what He wills of punishment and bliss, and He turns away our eyes and veils them from all of it because He is omnipotent over every possible thing.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage defines the reality and location of the punishment of the grave (adhab al-qabr). It states that the punishment affects both body and soul, by consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah, after the soul is returned to the body or a part thereof—addressing objections about bodily disintegration. It applies to disbelievers, hypocrites, and sinful Muslims. The proof is Quranic (Ghafir 40:46). It emphasizes rational possibility: if the intellect does not deem it impossible and revelation confirms it, belief is obligatory. God's power is unrestricted.

Two Types of Punishment of the Grave
Classifies punishment of the grave into perpetual and temporary, with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that punishment of the grave is classified into perpetual and temporary, with the temporary punishment capable of being lifted through supplication, charity, or other good deeds.

Core Idea
Punishment of the grave is not all the same; some is eternal, some can end.

The reality of the grave includes both reward and punishment. This lesson presents a key classification from the scholar Ibn al-Qayyim: punishment of the grave is not uniform. Some suffer perpetual torment, while others experience temporary punishment that can be removed. Understanding this distinction deepens our faith in the afterlife and clarifies the mercy of Allah towards sinful believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text and its English translation carefully. Notice the two categories mentioned: دائم (perpetual) and منقطع (temporary).
The author attributes this classification to Ibn al-Qayyim.
2
Identify the two types and their causes
Observe that perpetual punishment is for disbelievers and some sinners, while temporary punishment is for believers whose sins are light. Understand the basis for each.
3
Reflect on the removal of temporary punishment
Consider how temporary punishment can be lifted through supplication (du'a'), charity (sadaqah), or other good deeds. This highlights the importance of intercession and good works.
This is a source of hope for sinful believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعذاب القبر قسمان: ۱ - دائم ، وهو عذاب الكفار ، وبعض العصاة. ۲ - ومنقطع ، وهو عَذابُ مَن خَفَّت جرائمهم مِن العُصاة ؛ فإنَّهم يُعذِّبون بحَسَبها ، ثمَّ يُرفع عنهم بدعاء أو صدقة أو غير ذلك ، كما قاله ابن القيم .
And the punishment of the grave is of two types: 1 - Perpetual (da'im), and it is the punishment of the disbelievers and some sinners. 2 - And temporary (munqati'), and it is the punishment of those whose crimes are light from among the sinners; for they are punished according to them, then it is removed from them by supplication or charity or other than that, as Ibn al-Qayyim said.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage classifies the punishment of the grave into two types. The first is perpetual (da'im), which is for disbelievers and some sinners—these are punished indefinitely. The second is temporary (munqati'), for believers whose sins are light; they are punished proportionally, but the punishment can be lifted through supplication (du'a'), charity (sadaqah), or other means. The author attributes this distinction to Ibn al-Qayyim. The passage is a clear enumeration of the types and their causes.

منقطع
عذاب الكفار
عصاة المؤمنين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All punishment of the grave is eternal and cannot be removed.
Correction: The passage clarifies that only the punishment of disbelievers and some sinners is perpetual; for sinful believers, the punishment can be lifted through supplication, charity, and other good deeds.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Types and Definition of Punishment in the Grave
Classifies punishment in the grave into two types and defines it linguistically with a hadith proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two categories of punishment in the grave, the linguistic meaning of 'adhab, and the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Punishment in the grave is of two types, and its name shows its preventive purpose.

This passage from the Sam'iyyat section establishes that the punishment of the grave is not uniform. It differentiates between perpetual punishment for disbelievers and temporary punishment for light sinners, and then explains the linguistic root of 'adhab as striking and prevention. A terrifying hadith proves the reality of this punishment.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification
Identify the two types of punishment in the grave: perpetual and interrupted.
Perpetual is for disbelievers and some sinners; interrupted is for light sinners and lifted through supplication.
2
Learn the linguistic origin
Note that 'adhab originally means 'striking' and is used for any painful punishment because it prevents repetition.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Read the hadith about 99 snakes to understand the severity of punishment in the grave.
The author says this alone would be sufficient proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Realize that those not questioned in the grave are also not punished.
This connects the classification to earlier discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَن يُسأَلُ فِي قَبْرِهِ ومَن لا يُسأَل
۱ - دائم، وهو عذاب الكفار، وبعض العصاة.
۲ - ومنقطع، وهو عذاب من خفت جرائمهم من العصاة؛ فإنهم يعذبون بحسبها، ثم يرفع عنهم بدعاء أو صدقة أو غير ذلك، كما قاله ابن القيم.
قسم السمعيات
وأصل العذاب في كلام العرب الضرب، ثم استعمل في كل عقوبة مؤلمة، سمي عذابا لأنه يمنع المعاقب من معاودة مثل جرمه، ويمنع غيره من مثل فعله.
ومن عذاب القبر: ضغطته وهي التقاء حافتيه، ولو لم يكن من عذابه إلا ما خرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن ماجه عن أبي سعيد الخدري: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: (يسلط الله على الكافر في قبره تسعة وتسعين تنينا تنهشه وتلدغه حتى تقوم الساعة، ولو أن تنينا منها نفخ على الأرض ما أنبتت خضرا) لكان كافيا، وكل من ذكرنا أنه لا يسأل في قبره فكذلك لا يعذب فيه أيضا.
Who is questioned in his grave and who is not questioned. 1 - Perpetual, and it is the punishment of the disbelievers and some sinners. 2 - And interrupted, and it is the punishment of those whose crimes are light among the sinners; for they are punished according to them, then it is lifted from them by supplication or charity or other than that, as Ibn al-Qayyim said. Section of the Sam'iyyat (revealed matters). And the origin of 'adhab (punishment) in the speech of the Arabs is striking (al-darb), then it was used for every painful punishment; it is called 'adhab because it prevents the punished one from repeating the like of his crime, and it prevents others from the like of his action. And from the punishment of the grave: its squeezing (daghTatuhu), and it is the meeting of its two sides. And if there was not from its punishment except what Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say: 'Allah will empower over the disbeliever in his grave ninety-nine snakes that bite and sting him until the Hour is established, and if one of those snakes blew on the earth, it would not grow any greenery' – it would have been sufficient. And everyone we mentioned that he is not questioned in his grave, likewise he is not punished in it either.
Source pages p. 506

Commentary
This passage combines a classification, a linguistic definition, and a narrated proof regarding the punishment of the grave. It begins by stating the topic: who is questioned in the grave and who is not (the previous discussion is referenced). Then it classifies the punishment into two types: (1) perpetual punishment, which is for disbelievers and some sinners, and (2) interrupted punishment, which is for sinners with light crimes—they are punished accordingly until it is lifted through supplication, charity, or other means, as Ibn al-Qayyim stated. Next, the author introduces a new section, 'Sam'iyyat' (matters known only through revelation), and provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'adhab: its original meaning in Arabic is 'striking,' then it was extended to any painful punishment, and it is so called because it prevents (yaman'u) the punished person from repeating his crime and prevents others from doing the same. As a specific example of punishment in the grave, the author mentions 'daghTatuhu' (the squeezing of the grave), defined as the meeting of its two sides. He then cites a hadith from Ibn Abi Shayba and Ibn Majah via Abu Sa'id al-Khudri in which the Prophet ﷺ says that Allah will empower over the disbeliever in his grave ninety-nine snakes that bite and sting him until the Hour, and if one such snake blew on the earth, nothing green would grow. The author comments that even if only this hadith existed, it would be sufficient proof. Finally, he concludes that everyone previously mentioned as not being questioned in the grave is likewise not punished in it.

عذاب دائم
عذاب منقطع
ضغطة القبر
تنين
سمعيات

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage shows that light sinners also face temporary punishment which can be lifted.

Checkpoint

B) Prevention (al-man')
C) Pain (al-waja')

Key Takeaway
The punishment of the grave is varied: perpetual for disbelievers and temporary for light sinners, and it is proven by the linguistic root of 'adhab and the hadith of snakes.

?

?
The hadith says even one snake's breath would ruin the earth. How does this physical reality of the grave change the way you view your next hour? What will you do differently now?

Belief in the Bliss of the Grave: Obligation and Scope
States the obligation to believe in the bliss of the grave and its general application.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the bliss of the grave is obligatory and how its scope extends beyond the usual limitations of burial and responsibility.

Core Idea
The bliss of the grave is certain, universal, and not limited by burial or accountability.

Having established the reality of the grave's punishment, the author now turns to its counterpart: the bliss for believers. This lesson explains that the textual evidence for this bliss is so abundant it reaches tawatur (mass transmission), making belief in it obligatory. Moreover, the author clarifies that this blessing is not confined to Muslims of this nation, nor to those physically buried, nor even to those who were legally responsible during life — it extends to all who have died with faith, including those who lost their intellect.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the key term 'tawatur' and the three negations.
The passage is short but packed with theological implications.
2
Understand the proof
The passage uses the strength of tawatur to establish obligation. Why does tawatur make belief certain?
Tawatur means the reports are so widely transmitted that they yield certain knowledge.
3
Identify the three scope restrictions
The passage lists three things the bliss is not specific to. Find each: not only this ummah, not only the buried, not only the mukallaf. What does each clarify?
These restrictions expand the scope of the bliss beyond common assumptions.
4
Reflect on the inclusion of the non-responsible
The final point about 'the one whose intellect has ceased' shows that God's mercy extends even to those who never had legal responsibility. How does this shape our understanding of divine justice?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يجب الإيمان به أيضا: (نعيمه) أي: تنعيم الله تعالى المؤمنين في القبر؛ لما ورد في ذلك من النصوص البالغة مبلغ التواتر، ولا يختص بمؤمني هذه الأمة، كما أنه لا يختص بالمقبور، ولا بالمكلفين؛ فيكون لمن زال عقله.
And from what must be believed in also: His bliss, i.e., Allah's bestowing bliss upon the believers in the grave, due to what has been reported regarding that of texts reaching the level of tawatur (mass transmission), and it is not specific to the believers of this nation, just as it is not specific to the buried, nor to the legally responsible; thus it is for the one whose intellect has ceased.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage presents a separate doctrine concerning the grave: the bliss (na'im) that Allah bestows upon the believers. It states that belief in this bliss is obligatory (مما يجب الإيمان به). The proof is that the textual evidence for it has reached the level of tawatur (mass transmission), meaning it is certain and must be accepted. The author then clarifies three ways in which this bliss is not restricted: (1) it is not specific to the believers of this Muslim nation—past nations also experienced it; (2) it is not specific to those who are actually buried in a grave—the soul may experience it even if the body is not interred; (3) it is not specific to those who are legally responsible (mukallaf) — it includes those who have lost their intellect (e.g., children, the insane). Thus, the bliss of the grave is a universal divine favor for all believers.

Key Terms
نعيم القبر
تواتر
مؤمنون
مكلفون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the bliss of the grave is only for buried Muslims who were legally responsible.
Correction: The passage explicitly states it is not specific to the buried, not specific to the legally responsible, and not specific to this ummah, thus covering all believers.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the bliss of the grave is obligatory due to mass-transmitted texts, and it applies universally to all believers regardless of burial, nation, or legal responsibility.

Definition and Evidence of Grave Punishment
Author defines 'adhab and explains punishment in the grave with a hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic definition of 'adhāb, the specific punishment of the grave (including its pressure and the hadith of serpents), and the principle that those not questioned in the grave are not punished.

Core Idea
Grave punishment is real and proven by explicit hadith, not metaphorical.

In this lesson, we begin a new section on sam‘iyyāt, matters known only through revelation. The author first defines the term ‘adhāb linguistically, then presents specific evidence for the punishment of the grave. Understanding this establishes a foundational belief about the afterlife based on prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully, then the translation. Notice the structure: linguistic definition, then a single penalty (pressure of the grave), then a hadith reinforcing the reality.
The hadith is the core evidence.
2
Understand the linguistic root of ‘adhāb
The author explains that the original meaning of ‘adhāb is 'beating' and then generalized to any painful punishment that deters the criminal and others.
This shows the term has a concrete origin.
3
Identify the specific punishment described
The passage mentions the pressure of the grave (ḍaghṭat al-qabr) defined as the two sides meeting. Then the hadith about ninety-nine serpents biting the disbeliever until the Hour.
These are literal punishments, not symbolic.
4
Note the concluding rule
The author states that those who are not questioned in the grave (like children, the insane) are also not punished, linking accountability to punishment.
This is a consistent principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات وأصل العذاب في كلام العرب الضَّرب، ثمَّ استعمل في كُلِّ عُقوبةٍ مُؤلمة، سمّي عذابًا لأنَّه يَمنعُ المُعاقَب مِن مُعاوَدَة مثل جُرمِه، ويمنع غيرَهُ من مثل فعله. ومن عذاب القبر: ضَغْطَتُه وهي: التقاء حافتيه، ولو لم يكن من عذابه إلا ما خرجه ابن أبي شيبة وابن ماجه عن أبي سعيد الخدري قال: سمعتُ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: (يُسلط الله على الكافر في قبره تسعة وتسعين تِنِّينًا تَنْهَشُه وتَلْدَغُه حتَّى تقومَ السَّاعة، ولو أنَّ تِنّينًا منها نفخَ على الأرض ما أنبتتْ خَضِرًا) لكان كافيًا، وكلَّ مَن ذكرنا أنَّه لا يُسأل في قبره فكذلك لا يُعذَّب فيه أيضًا.
Section on sam‘iyyāt. The origin of ‘adhāb in the speech of the Arabs is beating, then it was used for every painful punishment, called ‘adhāb because it prevents the punished from repeating the like of his crime, and prevents others from the like of his action. Among the punishment of the grave is its pressure, which is the meeting of its two sides. And if there were nothing of its punishment except what Ibn Abī Shayba and Ibn Mājah narrated from Abū Sa‘īd al-Khudrī who said: I heard the Messenger of God ﷺ say: 'God will unleash upon the disbeliever in his grave ninety-nine serpents which bite and sting him until the Hour is established, and if one of those serpents blew on the earth, it would not grow any greenery' — that would be sufficient. And everyone we mentioned that he is not questioned in his grave, likewise he is not punished in it either.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage defines and provides evidence for the punishment of the grave. It begins by explaining the linguistic origin of the word ‘adhāb (punishment), which originally meant beating, then broadened to any painful deterrent punishment. The author then specifies one element of grave punishment: its pressure (ḍaghṭa), defined as the two sides of the grave coming together. To confirm the reality of this punishment, the author cites a hadith from Abū Sa‘īd al-Khudrī: the Prophet ﷺ stated that God will send ninety-nine serpents to bite and sting the disbeliever in his grave until the Day of Resurrection, emphasizing the horror by noting that a single serpent's breath would prevent vegetation. The author argues that even this single hadith would be sufficient proof, thus asserting the certainty of grave punishment based on textual evidence. The final sentence clarifies that those who are not questioned in the grave (e.g., children, the insane) are likewise not punished, showing a consistent link between accountability and punishment.
