The Obligation and Universal Scope of Grave Reward
Author states obligation of grave reward, its proof, and its universal scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in grave reward is obligatory, its basis in tawātur, and that it applies to all believers regardless of nation, burial, or mental state.

Core Idea
Grave reward is a universal truth for believers, proven by mass transmission.

Sanusi begins by establishing that grave reward is an article of faith supported by overwhelming scriptural evidence. He then clarifies that this reward is not limited to Muslims of this ummah, nor even to those buried in graves. This passage sets the universal scope of divine justice in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the structure: obligation, proof, scope.
2
Identify the proof
Find the term 'tawātur' and understand why it ensures certainty.
Mass transmission means the reports are undeniable.
3
Analyze the scope
Note the three negations: not exclusive to this ummah, not exclusive to burial, not exclusive to accountable adults.
This shows the reward is comprehensive for all believers.
4
Consider the mental state exception
The passage addresses those who lose their mind after adulthood; their state at loss determines outcome.
This reinforces that faith is the criterion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يجب الإيمان به أيضًا: (نَعِيمُهُ) أي: تنعيمُ اللهِ تعالى المؤمنينَ في القبر؛ لما ورد في ذلك مِن النُّصوص البالغة مبلَغَ التَّواتُر، ولا يختص بمؤمِنِي هذه الأمة، كما أنَّه لا يختص بالمقبور، ولا بالمُكلَّفين؛ فيكون لمن زال عقله أيضًا إذا مات بالغا، وتُعتبر الحالة التي زال عقله وهو عليها من كُفْرٍ وإيمان ونحوهما. ومن نعيمه تَوْسِيعُه، وجعل قنديل فيه، وفتح طاق فيه مِن الجَنَّة، وامتلاؤه بالرّيحان، وجعله روضة مِن رِيَاض الجنَّة، وكلُّ هذا محمولٌ على حقیقته عند العلماء.
And among what must be believed in is also: His reward, i.e., God’s bestowing bliss upon the believers in the grave, because of the texts that have reached the level of tawātur. And it is not exclusive to the believers of this ummah, just as it is not exclusive to the buried, nor to those accountable; so it is for one whose mind has ceased, also if he died as an adult, and the condition in which his mind ceased is considered: whether of disbelief, faith, or similar. Among its reward are: its widening, placing a lamp in it, opening a window in it from Paradise, filling it with basil, and making it a garden from the gardens of Paradise. All of this is taken in its literal sense according to the scholars.
Source pages p. 507

Commentary
This passage presents the reality of grave reward (na‘īm al-qabr) for believers. The author states that it is obligatory to believe in it because the scriptural proofs for it have reached the level of tawātur (mass transmission), ensuring certainty. He then clarifies that this reward is not limited to believers of the Muslim ummah alone—it applies to believers from previous nations as well. Moreover, it is not restricted to those who are physically buried in a grave; rather, it applies to all who die as believers, even if their bodies are not interred. It also applies to those who have lost their sanity after reaching adulthood, and the state at the time of loss (faith or disbelief) determines whether they receive reward or punishment. The author then enumerates specific blessings: the grave is expanded, a lamp is placed, a window to Paradise opens, it is filled with basil, and it becomes a garden of Paradise. These descriptions are understood literally by Sunni scholars, not metaphorically.

Key Terms
نعيم القبر
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think grave reward is only for Muslims of Prophet Muhammad's community.
Correction: The passage explicitly says it is not exclusive to the believers of this ummah, so it includes believers from all nations.

Checkpoint

A) Only Muslims of Prophet Muhammad's ummah
B) Only those who are buried in a grave
C) All believers, regardless of nation or burial
D) Only those who die as adults with full sanity

Key Takeaway
Belief in grave reward is obligatory based on mass-transmitted proofs, and it applies universally to all believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Author introduces the section on resurrection and begins explaining its obligation.

The Grave Events: Rational Possibility and Revealed Obligation
Sanusi describes grave bliss and states the ruling of rational possibility and revealed obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the events of the grave are rationally possible but become obligatory to believe based on revelation from the truthful Prophet.

Core Idea
Rational possibility plus truthful revelation equals binding belief.

Sanusi addresses a key category of Islamic theology: the sam'iyyat (matters known only through revelation). The events of the grave—questioning, bliss, and punishment—are not rationally necessary or impossible; they are possible. But because Allah's truthful Messenger informed us of them through the texts, they become obligatory to affirm. This lesson explores the description of these events and the logical-rational principle that makes them binding.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic, then the translation. Notice the specific details of grave bliss listed.
The passage uses a list format for the bliss elements.
2
Identify the ruling categories
Find where Sanusi says 'jā'iz 'aqlan wa wājib sam'an'. Understand each term and their significance.
Rationally possible means not impossible; obligatory by revelation means binding from scripture.
3
Trace the reasoning
Follow the logical chain: rationally possible → truthful informant → texts → obligation.
The principle is that reliable revelation converts possibility into duty.
4
Contrast with errors
Consider the common misconception that rational possibility implies no obligation. Sanusi explicitly counters this.
Belief is not optional when revelation confirms it.
5
Summarize the principle
Articulate the principle that rational possibility + revelation = binding belief.
This is the position of Ahl al-Sunna and most Mu'tazila.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالبعث وحشر الأجساد أيضًا إذا مات بالغا، وتُعتبر الحالة التي زال عقله وهو عليها من كفر وإيمان ونحوهما. ومن نعيمه توسيعه، وجعل قنديل فيه، وفتح طاق فيه من الجنة، وامتلاؤه بالريحان، وجعله روضة من رياض الجنة، وكل هذا محمول على حقيقته عند العلماء. وقوله (واجب) أي: ثابت سمعا، خبر «سؤالنا» وما عطف عليه، أي: كل واحد من الثلاثة المذكورة جائز عقلا واجب سمعا؛ لأنه أمر ممكن عقلا أخبر به الصادق على ما نطقت به النصوص، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو حق يجب قبوله شرعًا، على هذا أهل السنة وجمهور المعتزلة.
Faith in the resurrection and gathering of bodies also when one dies as an adult, and the state in which his mind ceased is considered upon him from disbelief and faith and the like. And from its bliss: its expansion, and making a lamp in it, and opening a window in it from Paradise, and filling it with basil, and making it a garden from the gardens of Paradise, and all of this is taken in its literal sense according to the scholars. And His saying (wājib) meaning: established by transmission (sam'an), predicate of 'our questioning' and what is coordinated with it, i.e., each of the three mentioned is rationally possible (jā'iz 'aqlan) and obligatory by transmission (wājib sam'an) because it is a matter rationally possible that the truthful one (al-sādiq) informed about according to what the texts have stated, and everything that is so is truth that must be accepted legally, upon this are Ahl al-Sunna and the majority of the Mu'tazila.
Source pages p. 508

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling regarding the events of the grave (the questioning, expansion, light, etc.). Sanusi first mentions the state of the deceased and the bliss of the grave. He then explains that the predicate "wājib" in the poem refers to these three matters (questioning, expansion, etc.) being obligatory by transmission (sam'an). They are rationally possible, and since the truthful Prophet informed us of them through revealed texts, they become legally obligatory to believe. This is the position of Ahl al-Sunna and most Mu'tazila. The passage thus establishes the epistemological principle that rational possibility combined with reliable revelation creates a binding belief.

Key Terms
بعث
حشر
جائز عقلا
واجب سمعا
الصادق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That rational possibility implies that belief in grave events is optional or not necessary.
Correction: Sanusi clarifies that rational possibility does not negate obligation; rather, because the truthful Prophet informed us through revelation, these events become legally binding to believe.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the ruling on the events of the grave?
A) Rationally impossible and forbidden to believe
B) Rationally possible and obligatory by revelation
C) Rationally necessary and optional to believe
D) Rationally possible but not obligatory

Key Takeaway
The events of the grave are rationally possible, but because the truthful Prophet informed us of them through revelation, believing in them becomes a binding obligation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The passage says the grave events are wājib sam'an—obligatory because the truthful Prophet informed us. Is your belief in the grave matters based on your own rational calculation or on your trust in the Messenger? Which one is stronger in your heart when doubts come?
?
Sanusi says the majority of Mu'tazila agree on this. But do you? Not as intellectual assent, but as a reality that will happen to your body tonight? If you knew for certain that your questioning begins tonight, would you be prepared? What is the one thing you need to fix before that moment?

The Definitions of Ba'th and Hashr
Sanusi defines ba'th and hashr and distinguishes them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of ba'th and hashr as taught by Imam Sanusi and the distinction between them.

Core Idea
Ba'th is revival; hashr is gathering—two distinct phases of resurrection.

In this passage, Imam Sanusi clarifies the terminology of resurrection. He distinguishes between ba'th (raising the dead) and hashr (gathering them for judgment). Understanding these terms is essential for grasping the later discussion about the nature of the resurrected body.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall meaning. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi defines both terms.
Pay attention to the distinction he makes.
2
Distinguish ba'th and hashr
Identify the two terms and note the specific actions they refer to: ba'th is revival, hashr is gathering.
3
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters for the overall doctrine of resurrection. How does understanding the phases help in later discussions?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشبه في الوجوب قوله: (كبعث الحشر) أي: كوجوب بعث الله جميع العباد وإعادتهم بعد إحيائهم بجميع أجزائهم الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، وسوقهم إلى محشرهم لفصل القضاء.

وقد فرق الإمام السنوسي بين البعث والحشر فقال: إن البعث عبارة عن إحياء الموتى وإخراجهم من قبورهم، والحشر: سوقهم جميعا إلى الموقف. فقوله: كوجوب بعث، أي: إحياء، والإضافة لأمته، أي: بعث الله الناس للحشر.

وقوله: (الأصلية) إشارة لرد شبهة من طرف المنكرين. قالوا لو أكل إنسان آخر وصار غذاء له ومن أجزاء بدنه، فالأجزاء المأكولة إما أن تعاد في بدن الأكل أو بدن المأكول، وأيا ما كان لا يكون أحدهما معادا بتمامه، على أنه لا أولوية لجعلها جزءا من بدن أحدهما دون الآخر، ولا سبيل إلى جعلها جزءا من كل منهما. وأيضا إذا كان الآكل كافرا والمأكول مؤمنا يلزم تنعيم الأجزاء العاصية أو تعذيب الأجزاء المطيعة. والجواب: أن الحشر للأجزاء الأصلية لا الحاصلة بالتغذية؛ فالمعاد من كل من الآكل والمأكول الأجزاء الأصلية الحاصلة في أول الفطرة من غير لزوم فساد. فإن قيل: يجوز أن تصير تلك الأجزاء الغذائية الأصلية في المأكول ذلك لا نطفة وأجزاء أصلية لبدن آخر ويعود المحذور. قلنا: المحذور إنما هو في وقوع إمكانه؛ فالله تعالى قادر أن يحفظها من أن تصير جزءا لبدن آخر فضلا عن أن تصير جزءا أصليا. اهـ.
And He likened in obligation His saying: (like the resurrection of the gathering) meaning: like the obligation of God raising all servants and returning them after their revival with all their original parts (ajzā'ihim al-aṣliyya), which are those that are meant to persist from the beginning of life to its end, and driving them to their gathering place for the passing of judgment. And Imam Sanusi distinguished between ba'th and hashr, saying: ba'th is reviving the dead and bringing them out of their graves, and hashr is driving them all to the standing place. So His saying: like the obligation of raising, i.e., reviving, and the addition [of God] to His community, i.e., God raising people for the gathering. And His saying: (original) is a reference to refuting a doubt from the deniers. They said: if one person eats another and it becomes nourishment for him and part of his body, then the eaten parts are either returned in the body of the eater or the body of the eaten, and in either case one of them is not fully returned, with no priority to make them part of one body over the other, and there is no way to make them part of both. Also if the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten is a believer, it would necessitate giving bliss to the disobedient parts or punishing the obedient parts. The answer: the gathering is for the original parts, not those acquired through nutrition; so the restored person from each of the eater and the eaten are the original parts present at the first creation without corruption. If it is said: it is possible that those nutritional parts become original parts for another body and the problem returns. We say: the problem is only in the occurrence of its possibility; God is able to preserve them from becoming part of another body, let alone becoming an original part.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage first clarifies that the obligation of resurrection is similar to the obligation of the grave events. It then defines ba'th as reviving the dead and bringing them out of graves, and hashr as driving them to the standing place. The main point is that resurrection involves only the original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya) that persist from birth to death, not parts acquired through nutrition. This serves to refute the objection of the deniers that if a person eats another, the body parts would be shared. The objection argues that if a disbeliever eats a believer, the same parts would have to be either punished or rewarded, leading to contradiction. The answer is that the resurrection is only for the original parts present at the first creation; God is able to preserve those original parts from being assimilated into another body. Even if it is possible that nutritional parts become original for another, God can prevent that. The passage also notes that this refutes the charge of reincarnation (tanasukh).

حشر

D) Ba'th is for believers, hashr for disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Imam Sanusi defines ba'th as reviving the dead and hashr as gathering them for judgment, two distinct phases of the resurrection.

Do you truly believe that you will one day wake up from your grave, body intact, and stand before Allah? How would you live differently today if this reality were fully embedded in your heart?
?
The passage says hashr is the driving of all to the standing place for judgment. Nothing can stop that procession. Are you ready for that journey? What specific action will you take this week to prepare for the moment you will be gathered?

The Original Parts Condition and Refutation of the Doubt
Sanusi refutes the doubt about cannibalism by specifying original parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition that resurrection involves only original parts and how this refutes the doubt about shared body parts from cannibalism.

Core Idea
Only original parts are resurrected; acquired parts do not create contradiction.

A common objection to bodily resurrection involves the case of cannibalism: if one person eats another, whose body do the parts belong to? Imam Sanusi refutes this by clarifying that resurrection applies only to the original parts present from birth. This lesson examines the doubt and the theological response.

Guided Path
1
Understand the doubt
Read the doubt presented by the deniers. They argue about shared body parts and contradictory rewards or punishments.
Notice the two aspects: the physical sharing and the ethical problem.
2
Learn Sanusi's answer
Read Sanusi's response: resurrection is for the original parts only, not the acquired ones.
This solves both aspects.
3
Consider the counter-objection
A possible counter is raised: what if acquired parts become original for another? Sanusi responds that God can prevent that.
Reflect on the reliance on divine power.

Resurrection and the Original Parts
Sanusi defines ba'th and hashr and explains the condition of original parts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection in Islam applies only to the original parts that persist from birth, not to parts acquired through nutrition, and how this answers the cannibal objection.

Core Idea
Only original parts are resurrected; nutrition does not create a problem for bodily resurrection.

The passage clarifies two key eschatological terms—ba'th (resurrection) and hashr (gathering)—and addresses a classic objection: if a cannibal eats another person, how can both be resurrected fully? Sanusi explains the crucial qualification that resurrection concerns only the original parts present at the beginning of life, not those acquired through nutrition. This allows a coherent response to the objection while preserving the doctrine of bodily resurrection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the technical terms and the flow from definition to objection to answer.
2
Identify the core definition
Find how the passage defines ba'th and hashr: it is the return of all servants with all their original parts and their gathering for judgment. Note the correction of word order mentioned in the commentary.
The phrase 'original parts' is key.
3
Understand the cannibal objection
Read the objection: if one person eats another, the eaten parts become part of the eater. How can both be resurrected completely? The passage presents the objection and then the answer.
This objection challenges the coherence of bodily resurrection.
4
Study the answer and its implications
The answer is that resurrection is for the original parts, not those acquired through nutrition. God preserves those original parts from being permanently absorbed. Also note the clarification about parts like nails and saliva not being resurrected.
This preserves divine justice and avoids dilemmas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات جميع العباد وإعادتهم بعد إحيائهم بجميع أجزائهم الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، وسوقهم إلى محشرهم لفصل القضاء بينهم.

قوله: ( وإعادتهم بعد إحيائهم في العبارة قلب، والأصل: وإحيائهم بعد إعادتهم بجميع أجزائهم. الأمير.

قوله: (الأصلية) إشارة لرد شبهة من طرف المنكرين، قالوا لو أكل إنسان آخر؛ وصار غذاء له ومن أجزاء بدنه؛ فالأجزاء المأكولة إما أن تعاد في بدن الأكل أو بدن المأكول، وأيا ما كان لا يكون أحدهما معادا بتمامه، على أنه لا أولوية لجعلها جزءا من بدن أحدهما دون الآخر، ولا سبيل إلى جعلها جزءا من كل منهما، وأيضا إذا كان الآكل كافرا والمأكول مؤمنا يلزم تنعيم الأجزاء العاصية أو تعذيب الأجزاء المطيعة. والجواب: أن الحشر للأجزاء الأصلية لا الحاصلة بالتغذية؛ فالمعاد من كل من الآكل والمأكول الأجزاء الأصلية الحاصلة في أول الفطرة من غير لزوم فساد، فإن قيل: يجوز أن تصير تلك الأجزاء الغذائية الأصلية في المأكول ذلك لا نطفة وأجزاء أصلية لبدن آخر ويعود المحذور. قلنا: المحذور إنما هو في وقوع إمكانه؛ فالله تعالى قادر أن يحفظها من أن تصير جزءا لبدن آخر فضلا عن أن تصير جزءا أصليا. اهـ. من شرح المقاصد.

قوله: (وهي التي من شأنها البقاء) أي: وهي التي كانت موجودة حال نفخ الروح فيه، ولو قطعت قبل موته، والقول أنه يقبح أن ينالها ما حدث بعدها مردود بأنها تابعة، والمقصود: الشخص بروحه وجسمه في الجملة، واحترز به عما شأنه عدم البقاء، فإنا لا نلتزم إعادته، كالظفر والبصاق. الأمير والشنواني.

قوله: (من أول العمر) ولو الغرلة، وهي قلفة الختان، حيث ورد أنهم يحشرون غرلا.
Section of revealed matters. All servants and their return after their resurrection with all their original parts, and they are those whose nature is to persist from the beginning of life to its end, and their driving to their gathering place for the separation of judgment between them.

His saying: (And their return after their resurrection) in the expression is inversion, and the original is: and their resurrection after their return with all their parts. al-Amir.

His saying: (original) is an indication to refute an obscurity from the side of the deniers. They said: if one human eats another, and it becomes nutrition for him and from parts of his body, then the eaten parts are either returned in the eater's body or the eaten's body, and in either case neither of them is returned completely, especially since there is no preference for making them part of one body over the other, nor is there a way to make them part of each body. Also, if the eater is a disbeliever and the eaten is a believer, it would necessitate delighting the disobedient parts or punishing the obedient parts. The answer: the gathering is for the original parts, not those acquired through nutrition; so what is returned from each of the eater and the eaten is the original parts that came to be at the beginning of creation without necessitating corruption. If it is said: it is possible that those nutritional parts become original parts in the eaten (as a nutfa and original parts for another body) and the problem returns. We say: the problem is only in the occurrence of its possibility; so God Almighty is able to preserve them from becoming a part for another body, let alone becoming an original part. End quote from Sharh al-Maqasid.

His saying: (and they are those whose nature is to persist) i.e., they are those that existed at the time of the blowing of the spirit into him, even if cut off before his death. And the statement that it is repugnant that what happens after them should affect them is rejected because they are subordinate. The intended meaning: the person by his spirit and body in general. And he differentiated by it from what has the nature of non-persistence, for we do not commit to its return, like the nail and saliva. al-Amir and al-Shanawani.

His saying: (from the beginning of life) even the foreskin, which is the prepuce of circumcision, as it has been reported that they are gathered with foreskins.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage defines the resurrection (ba'th) and gathering (hashr) and explains the crucial condition of original parts (al-ajza' al-asliyya). The author first states the revealed belief: all people will be returned to life after death with all their original parts — those that persist from the beginning of life to the end — and driven to the place of judgment. The word order in the text is noted as inverted (قلب), with the proper order being 'their resurrection after their return'. The specification of 'original parts' is a response to an objection raised by deniers: the cannibal problem. The objection and answer are detailed: if a cannibal eats another human, how can both be resurrected completely? The answer is that resurrection applies only to the original parts present at the beginning of creation, not those acquired through nutrition. A further objection is considered: what if the original parts of the eaten person become part of the eater's body and then original for him? The answer is that God preserves those parts from becoming original for another. Then the passage clarifies what counts as original (parts existing at the soul's blowing, including the foreskin, but excluding nails and saliva). This is a definition combined with a refutation, following the author's argumentative order, preserving the nuance of body, soul, and divine power.

أجزاء أصلية
إعادة
شبهة الأكل

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that bodily resurrection impossible if corpses mix or are eaten.
Correction: Only original parts (present at creation) are resurrected; God preserves them intact.

Checkpoint

B) Resurrection is only for the original parts, not for parts acquired through nutrition.
C) The eater is not resurrected because he committed a sin.

Key Takeaway
Bodily resurrection applies only to the original parts present at the beginning of life; this answers apparent dilemmas like cannibalism and ensures divine justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your body has changed many times through eating and growth, do you trust that the One who created you from nothing can restore your true self for judgment? What does that trust demand from you today?
?
The deniers argued that bodily resurrection is impossible because of apparent contradictions. Are there any doubts in your heart about Allah's power to resurrect you exactly as you are accountable? What would it mean to live with absolute certainty of standing before Him?
?
The original parts are those present at the moment the soul was breathed into you. If your identity is tied to that first creation, how should you view the changes and losses your body endures? Does this change how you treat your body or how you prepare for the next life?

Refuting the Reincarnation Objection
The author refutes the claim that resurrecting from original parts implies reincarnation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author defends resurrection against the charge of reincarnation by distinguishing between a body created from original parts and a completely new body.

Core Idea
Resurrection from original parts is not reincarnation; it is a verbal dispute.

This passage addresses a common objection against bodily resurrection: that rebuilding a body from its original matter is tantamount to reincarnation. The author, using a commentary on 'Aqa'id al-Nasafi, clarifies the precise condition that would make it reincarnation and why the Islamic view avoids it.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Start by reading the objection in the source. Notice how it cites hadith descriptions to argue that the resurrected body differs from the earthly one, implying reincarnation.
The objection uses physical differences as evidence.
2
Identify the author's key distinction
The author responds by stating that reincarnation would only follow if the second body is NOT created from the original parts of the first. This is the critical condition that separates resurrection from reincarnation.
The word 'original parts' (أجزاء أصلية) is central.
3
Understand the conclusion
If someone still calls it reincarnation, it becomes a verbal dispute. The proofs for resurrection apply regardless of the name.
The author emphasizes substance over terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال في شرح عقائد النسفي: فإن قيل: هذا قول بالتناسخ؛ البدن الثاني ليس هو الأول، لما ورد في الحديث من أن أهل الجنة جرد مرد، وأن الجهنمي ضرسه مثل جبل أحد، ومن ههنا قال من قال: ما من مذهب إلا وللتناسخ فيه قدم راسخ. قلنا: إنما يلزم التناسخ لو لم يكن البدن الثاني مخلوقا من الأجزاء الأصلية للبدن الأول؛ وإن سمي مثل ذلك تناسخا كان نزاعا في مجرد الاسم، ولا دليل على استحالة إعادة الروح إلى مثل هذا البدن، بل الأدلة القائمة على حقيقته سواء تناسخا أو لا. اهـ.
And he said in Sharh Aqa'id al-Nasafi: For if it is said: This is a statement of reincarnation; the second body is not the first, because it has come in the hadith that the people of Paradise are beardless and hairless, and that the tooth of the Hell-dweller is like Mount Uhud, and from here one who said said: There is no sect but that in it reincarnation has a firm footing. We say: Reincarnation would only follow if the second body were not created from the original parts of the first body; and if such a thing is called reincarnation, it is a dispute over a mere name, and there is no proof for the impossibility of returning the soul to such a body, rather the proofs that exist for its reality are the same whether it is reincarnation or not. End quote.
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage defending the resurrection of original parts from the charge of reincarnation (tanasukh). The objection states that if the resurrected body is made from original parts of the first body, it is a different body, thus implying reincarnation – citing hadiths about physical differences in the afterlife. The answer clarifies that reincarnation would only follow if the second body were NOT created from the first body's original parts. If one still calls it reincarnation, it is a mere verbal dispute. There is no proof that returning the soul to such a body is impossible; the proofs for resurrection apply whether one calls it reincarnation or not. The passage preserves the nuance that the identity of the body is tied to its original matter.

Key Terms

أجزاء أصلية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any return of the soul to a material body made from previous parts constitutes reincarnation.
Correction: Reincarnation only occurs if the body is not created from the original parts of the first body. Resurrection from original parts avoids that.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when would resurrection be considered reincarnation (tanasukh)?
A) When the second body is created from the original parts of the first.
B) When the second body is not created from the original parts of the first.
C) When the soul is returned to a non-material body.
D) When there is any physical change in the body.

Key Takeaway
Resurrection from original parts is not reincarnation; the distinction hinges on whether the body is made from the original matter or entirely new matter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What would it take for you to honestly reconsider?
?
The author says that if someone insists on calling resurrection from original parts 'reincarnation', it becomes a mere verbal dispute. Are there aspects of your faith that you hold onto because of the label, rather than the reality behind it? Would you be willing to let go of a cherished term if the core truth remains unchanged?
?
The proofs for resurrection stand regardless of whether it is called reincarnation or not. Is your certainty in the resurrection based on evidence and rational conviction, or on how comfortably it fits into your existing categories? Examine your heart: are you attached to the name or the reality?

The Scriptural and Consensual Proof of Resurrection
The author affirms resurrection as a revealed truth via three sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection is a revealed truth, not a rational necessity, established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.

Core Idea
Resurrection is a truth revealed by the Lawgiver, made certain through revelation.

This lesson examines how classical Sunni theology grounds belief in resurrection. The author asserts that resurrection is a truth firmly established by divine revelation and the consensus of the early community. You will see why this belief is not a matter of rational proof but of trusting the Lawgiver's report.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the key terms and the flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the phrase 'everything that is so is established'.
2
Identify the three sources
The passage mentions Book, Sunnah, and consensus. Notice how the author presents them as the evidential foundation.
3
Understand the epistemological point
The passage insists that resurrection is among the 'possibilities' (mumkinat) that the Lawgiver has reported. This means its certainty comes from revelation, not reason alone.
This counters the misconception that resurrection must be rationally necessary.
4
Reflect on al-Amir's critique
The commentary notes a logical weakness in phrasing: the author appears to use the claim as evidence. Yet the overall point remains valid.
Why might this critique matter for a student of kalam?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالبعث وحشر الأجساد السلف، مع القضاء بينهم، إذ هذا كله حق ثابت بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع كونه من الممكنات التي أخبر بها الشارع، وكل ما هو كذلك فهو ثابت، والإخبار عنه مطابق. وفي القرآن: قال من يحيي العظام وهي رميم [يس: 78] الآية، كما بدأنا أول خلق نعيده [الأنبياء: 104].

قوله: (إذ هذا كله حق .. إلى قوله: التي أخبر بها الشارع) لا يخفى الركة، فإنه أخذ الدعوى وهي الحقيقة في الدليل، وأعاد ما قبل مع ما بعدها؛ فإن الثبوت بالكتاب.. الخ هو إخبار الشارع. الأمير.
Belief in the resurrection and gathering of bodies, with judgment between them, for all this is a truth firmly established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, it being among the possibilities that the Lawgiver has reported; and everything that is so is established, and the report about it corresponds [to reality]. And in the Qur'an: He said: 'Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?' [Ya Sin 78] the verse, 'As We began the first creation We will repeat it' [al-Anbiya 104].

His saying: (for all this is a truth ... up to his saying: that the Lawgiver has reported) is not hidden [that it is] weak, because he took the claim — which is the reality — as the evidence, and repeated what came before with what came after it; for the establishment by the Book, etc. is the report of the Lawgiver. al-Amir.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for resurrection as a matter of faith. It states that belief in resurrection and bodily gathering is a truth established by three sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, and the consensus (ijma) of the Salaf. It further asserts that resurrection is among the possibilities (mumkinat) that the Lawgiver has informed us about; and whatever the Lawgiver informs about is true and corresponds to reality. Two Quranic verses are cited as evidence: 'Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?' (Yasin 78) and 'As We began the first creation We will repeat it' (al-Anbiya 104). The footnote by al-Amir criticizes the phrasing of the argument, noting that it appears to take the claim itself as evidence, but the point remains that the proof is ultimately the divine report. The passage is a concise statement of the epistemological basis for belief in resurrection.

Misconception: Resurrection must be rationally necessary or provable by reason alone.
Correction: The passage classifies resurrection as a 'possible' (mumkin) that becomes certain only through the truthful report of the Lawgiver, not through rational demonstration.

Resurrection of All Creatures: Proofs from Hadith and Reason
The author presents two opinions on who is resurrected, favoring the inclusion of all.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence from the Quran and Sunnah that all creatures, including animals, will be resurrected, and how the objection about moral responsibility is answered.

Core Idea
All creatures will be gathered on the Day of Resurrection for Divine justice, whether morally responsible or not.

This lesson explores a key aspect of Islamic eschatology: the scope of resurrection. While many assume only humans are resurrected, the Prophet ﷺ taught that even animals will be gathered. We will examine the two scholarly opinions and the evidence that supports the majority view.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get an overview of the content.
Notice the two opinions and the hadith mentioned.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage presents the view of the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) and al-Nawawi that all creatures are resurrected, and a dissenting group that only the recompensed are gathered.
The author sides with the former.
3
Examine the evidence from hadith
The hadith about the hornless and horned sheep proves that animals are gathered. Reflect on how this is a clear proof.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and is considered agreed upon.
4
Understand the objection and answer
An objection is raised that animals are not morally responsible, so why gather them? The answer: they are gathered for justice among themselves, not for sin.
This shows that resurrection is not only for punishment but also for establishing justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا فرق في ذلك بين من يحاسب كالمكلف ولا غيره على ما ذهب إليه المحققون وصححه النووي واختاره، وذهبت طائفة: إلى أنه لا يحشر إلا من يجازى.

قوله: (ولا غيره) كالبهائم والوحوش؛ ففي صحيح مسلم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «لتؤدن الحقوق إلى أهلها يوم القيامة، حتى يقاد للشاة الجماء من الشاة القرناء» فدل هذا على أن البهائم تحشر يوم القيامة. فإن قلت: غير الإنسان من ذي الروح لا يجري عليه القلم فلا يؤاخذ. أجيب بأنه يؤاخذ فيما بينه وبين نظيره تحقيقا للعدل، لا لارتكاب ذنب. الشنواني.

[متفق عليه] بضم المعجمة بعدها مهملة ساكنة. الأمير والشنواني.
There is no difference in that between one who is judged, like the morally responsible person, and others, according to what the verifiers went to and al-Nawawi corrected and chose; and a group went to that none is gathered except one who is recompensed.

His saying: (and others) such as beasts and wild animals; for in Sahih Muslim that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Rights will certainly be rendered to their owners on the Day of Resurrection, until the hornless sheep is avenged from the horned sheep.' So this indicates that beasts are gathered on the Day of Resurrection. If you say: Other than humans among living beings are not subject to the pen (i.e., moral responsibility), so they are not punished. It is answered: They are punished in what is between them and their like for the realization of justice, not for committing sin. al-Shanawani.

Commentary
This passage discusses the scope of resurrection: who is gathered on the Day of Judgment. The author states the position of the verifiers (al-muhaqqiqun) and al-Nawawi that there is no difference between the morally responsible (mukallaf) and others—all are resurrected. A dissenting group holds that only those who will be recompensed (i.e., the judged) are gathered. The footnote clarifies 'others' includes beasts and wild animals, citing the hadith about the hornless sheep being avenged from the horned sheep, which proves animals are gathered. A potential objection is raised: animals are not morally responsible, so why would they be gathered? The answer is that they are gathered for justice among themselves, not for punishment for sin. The hadith is classified as 'agreed upon' (muttafaq 'alayhi). The passage thus presents a classification of opinions and a supporting argument.

The Meaning of 'Easier' in Divine Resurrection
The author clarifies that divine reuse is called easier relative to creatures' abilities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the act of repeating creation is called 'easier' for Allah and how this relates to the recipient's preparedness, not a difference in divine power.

Core Idea
Divine reuse is called easier not because God's power varies, but because of the recipient's readiness.

The Quran describes the repetition of creation as 'easier' upon Allah, which raises a theological question: if Allah's power is eternal and all acts are equal for Him, how can one act be easier? This passage from al-Maqasid provides a precise answer by distinguishing between ease from the agent's side and ease from the recipient's side. We'll explore this distinction and its implications for understanding divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage first, then the translation. Pay attention to the objection about God's power and the response that follows.
The objection is based on the assumption that God's power is uniform for all acts.
2
Identify the two aspects of ease
The answer distinguishes ease from the agent's side (conditions of agency) and from the recipient's side (preparedness). Notice which one is intended here.
3
Understand the comparative form
The passage notes that the comparative 'af'ala al-tafdil' is not used in its usual literal sense but contextually relative to human custom. Al-Baydawi's quote reinforces this.
This preserves God's transcendence while explaining the verse's language.
4
Reflect on the overall point
Consider how this explanation upholds both the Quranic text and the theological principle that God's power is perfect and unchanging.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدة: قوله تعالى: {وَهُوَ الَّذِى يَبْدَؤُا الْخَلْقَ ثُمَّ يُعِيدُهُ، وَهُوَ أَهْوَنُ عَلَيْهِ} [الروم: 27]. قال في المقاصد. فإن قيل: ما معنى كون الإعادة أهون على الله تعالى وقدرته قديمة لا تتفاوت المقدورات بالنسبة لها؟ قلنا: كون الفعل أهون تارة يكون من جهة الفاعل بزيادة شرائط الفاعلية، وتارة من جهة القابل بزيادة استعدادات القبول، وهذا هو المراد هنا، وأما من جهة قدرة الفاعل فالكل على السواء. اهـ. بالحرف، واشتهر الاقتصار على أن أفعل التفضيل هنا على غير بابه فحاصله {كَمَا بَدَأْنَا أَوَّلَ خَلْقٍ نُعِيدُهُ} [الأنبياء: 104] وإنما ألزموا بظاهر المألوف لهم، قال القاضي البيضاوي: والإعادة أسهل من الأصل بالإضافة إلى قدركم والقياس على أصولكم، ولذا قيل: الهاء للخلق. اهـ فتدبر. الأمير.
Benefit: His saying, exalted: {And He is the One who begins creation and then repeats it, and it is easier upon Him} [al-Rum 27]. He said in al-Maqasid: For if it is said: What is the meaning of the repetition being easier upon God Almighty while His power is eternal and objects of power do not differ in relation to it? We say: The act being easier sometimes is from the aspect of the agent by increase of conditions of agency, and sometimes from the aspect of the recipient by increase of preparedness of reception, and that is what is intended here. As for the aspect of the agent's power, all are equal. End quote verbatim. And it is commonly restricted to the fact that the comparative (af'ala al-tafdil) here is not used in its usual sense, so its sum is {As We began the first creation We will repeat it} [al-Anbiya 104]; they only obliged them by the apparent in accordance with their familiar custom. al-Qadi al-Baydawi said: And the repetition is easier than the origin relative to your power and analogy upon your principles. Therefore it was said: the pronoun (ha) refers to creation. End quote, so reflect. al-Amir.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage addresses an objection regarding the verse 'and it is easier upon Him' (al-Rum 27). The objection asks: how can the act of repetition be easier for God, given that His power is eternal and all objects of power are equal before it? The answer distinguishes two aspects: ease can be from the agent's side (by increase in conditions of agency) or from the recipient's side (by increase in preparedness to receive). Here it is from the recipient's side; from the aspect of God's power, all acts are equal. A common interpretation is that the comparative form (af'ala al-tafdil) is not used in its usual sense but rather indicates that, according to human custom and experience, repeating something is easier than beginning it. Al-Baydawi clarifies that this is relative to human capacity and analogy. The pronoun 'it' in 'easier upon Him' is said to refer to 'creation' (al-khalq). The passage ends with a call to reflect, indicating the subtlety of the issue.

إعادة
قادر
شروط الفاعلية
استعدادات القبول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that God's power is subject to degrees of ease or difficulty.
Correction: Ease is in the recipient's preparedness, not in divine power; God's power is equally capable of all acts.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the repetition of creation called 'easier' regarding God?
A) Because God's power for the second act is greater.
B) Because of the greater preparedness of the recipient, not ease in God's power.
C) Because the first creation was harder for God.
D) Because God is less involved in the second creation.

Key Takeaway
The act of reuse is called easier relative to the recipient's preparedness, not due to any variation in Allah's power.

Proof of Resurrection and the Dispute on Who Is Gathered
Sanusi proves resurrection by divine information and presents the dispute on universality of gathering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection is proven by divine information and that there is a dispute on whether all creatures or only accountable humans are gathered.

Core Idea
Resurrection is true by Allah's report; all beings will be gathered for justice.

In this passage, Sanusi presents the proof for resurrection and then addresses a scholarly dispute on the universality of the gathering. He shows that resurrection is a possible matter that Allah has informed us about, and that the Lawgiver's report is necessarily true. He then explains that the majority of scholars, including al-Nawawi, hold that all creatures—including animals—will be gathered for judgment, while a minority limit gathering to those who will be recompensed. He supports the majority view with a hadith about animals being judged.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get an overview of the argument and the dispute.
Notice the footnote numbers (1) and (3).
2
Understand the proof for resurrection
Identify the logical structure: resurrection is a possible thing that Allah informed about, so it is true. The Qur'anic verses confirm Allah's power to recreate.
3
Examine the dispute on gathering
Notice the two views: majority (all creatures) and minority (only recompensed). See how the hadith supports the majority.
The hadith is about animals getting retaliation.
4
Consider the objections and responses
Read footnote (3) which addresses the objection that animals are not accountable. Understand the answer: they are judged for justice among themselves, not for sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بالبعث وحشر الأجساد السَّلف ، مع القضاء بينهم، إذ هذا كُلَّه حقٌّ ثابت بالكتاب والسُّنَّة وإجماع كونه من المُمكنات التي أخبر بها الشَّارع (۱) ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فهو ثابت، والإخبار عنه مُطابق . وفي القرآن: قَالَ مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَامَ وَهِيَ رَمِيم [يس: ۷۸] الآية ، كما بَدَأْنَا أَوَّلَ خَلْقِ نُعِيدُهُ [الأنبياء: ١٠٤] ، لا فرق في ذلك بين مَن يُحاسب كالمُكلَّف ولا غيره (۳) على ما ذهب إليه المُحققون وصححه النووي واختاره ، وذهبتْ طائفةٌ : إلى أنَّه لا يُحشَر إِلَّا مَن يُجازى. (۱) قوله: (إذ هذا كله حق ... إلى قوله : التي أخبر بها الشارع لا يخفى الركة ، فإنه أخذ الدعوى وهي الحقيقة ـ في الدليل، وأعاد ما قبل مع ما بعدها ؛ فإنَّ الثبوت بالكتاب... الخ هو إخبار الشارع . الأمير . (۳) قوله: (ولا غيره) كالبهائم والوحوش ؛ ففي صحيح مسلم أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «التؤدنَّ الحقوق إلى أهلها يوم القيامة، حتى يُقاد للشاة الجماء من الشاة القرناء فدل هذا على أنَّ البهائم تُحشرُ يوم القيامة. فإن قلت: غير الإنسان من ذي الروح لا يجري عليه القلم فلا يؤاخذ. أجيب بأنه يؤاخذ فيما بينه وبين نظيره تحقيقا للعدل ، لا لارتكاب ذنب . الشنواني .
Faith in the resurrection and gathering of bodies, and the judgment between them, for all this is a truth established by the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, being among the possible things which the Lawgiver informed about (1), and everything that is like that is true, and the information about it is accurate. And in the Qur'an: He said: 'Who will give life to bones while they are decayed?' [Ya-Sin:78] the verse, and 'As We began the first creation, We will repeat it' [Al-Anbiya:104]. There is no difference in that between one who is held to account, like the morally responsible person, and others (3), according to what the verifiers held and al-Nawawi authenticated and chose, and a group went to the view that only one who is recompensed will be gathered. (1) His statement: 'For all this is truth... up to his statement: which the Lawgiver informed about' — the slackness is not hidden, for he took the claim, which is the truth, as the evidence, and repeated what came before with what comes after it; for the establishment by the Book etc. is the Lawgiver's information. Al-Amir. (3) His statement: 'and others' like beasts and wild animals; for in Sahih Muslim that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Rights will certainly be restored to their owners on the Day of Resurrection, until the hornless sheep is retaliated for from the horned sheep' — so this indicates that beasts are gathered on the Day of Resurrection. If you say: non-human sentient beings are not subject to the Pen, so they are not punished. It is answered: they are punished with regard to what is between them and their kind for the realization of justice, not for committing a sin. Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the resurrection and gathering of bodies, and then addresses a dispute about who is gathered. The author begins by stating that belief in resurrection and gathering is a truth established by three sources: the Book (Qur'an), the Sunnah, and consensus. He explains that resurrection is among the possible things that the Lawgiver (i.e., Allah through revelation) has informed about; anything that has been informed about by the Lawgiver is necessarily true, and the information corresponds to reality. He then cites two Qur'anic verses as evidence: the first from Surah Ya-Sin where the disbeliever asks who can give life to decayed bones, and the second from Surah al-Anbiya' where Allah says 'as We began the first creation, We will repeat it.' The argument is that just as Allah created the first time, He can recreate. The author then presents a dispute: the majority of verifiers, including al-Nawawi, hold that all people — including animals — will be gathered for judgment, with no distinction between those who are morally accountable and others (like animals). A minority group holds that only those who will be recompensed (i.e., humans accountable for deeds) will be gathered. A footnote (1) by al-Amir critiques the phrasing of the proof, noting a potential circularity: the claim that resurrection is true is supported by the fact that it is in the Book, etc., but that is essentially the same as saying the Lawgiver informed about it — the evidence and the claim seem to overlap. Another footnote (3) by al-Shanwani explains the view of the majority, citing a hadith from Sahih Muslim about animals being gathered for retaliation, and addresses the objection that non-human animals are not subject to religious law, answering that their punishment is for justice among themselves, not for sin.

Key Terms
البعث
الحشر
الممكنات
إخبار الشارع
السلف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Resurrection is proven by rational possibility alone.
Correction: The passage says resurrection is proven because it is among the possible things that Allah informed about; the divine information is the basis.

Checkpoint

Ruling on Miscarriage in Resurrection
Sanusi states the ruling on miscarriage: if spirit was blown, it is resurrected; otherwise like inanimate matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the criterion for resurrection of a miscarriage based on whether the spirit was blown into it.

Core Idea
Resurrection requires a spirit; miscarriages without spirit are not resurrected.

This lesson examines a specific case in eschatology: the fate of miscarriages. Imam Sanusi clarifies that the determining factor is whether the fetus received the spirit (at 120 days). If so, it is resurrected and enters Paradise; otherwise, it is treated as inanimate matter and turns to dust. This ruling illustrates how kalam applies principles to particular instances.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to get the literal meaning.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if ... then ...; otherwise ...'.
2
Identify the condition and two outcomes
Find the condition (after spirit blown or not) and the two outcomes (resurrected vs. like inanimate matter).
The condition is binary: either the spirit was blown or not.
3
Understand the rationale
Ask why the spirit is the decisive factor. The hadith places spirit at 120 days; resurrection requires spiritual existence.
This connects to the broader Islamic belief that souls are resurrected.
4
Reflect on eschatological implications
Consider what this ruling says about divine justice and the gathering of all creation.
Inanimate matter is gathered only to be turned to dust, not given eternal existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأمَّا السِّقْطُ (۱) ؛ فإن أُلقي بعد نفخ الروح فيه بُعِثَ (٢)، وإلا كان كسائر الموات (۳). (۱) قوله : (السقط) أي: الذي لم تتم له ستة أشهر . الشنواني . (۲) قوله : (بعث) أي: أُعيد بروحه، ويصير عند دخول الجنة كأهلها في الجمال والطول. الشنواني . (۳) قوله : (المَوَات) بفتحتين مُخففا كالجَمَاد ، وهو الجسم الذي لا روح له، كالحجر ؛ فيُحشُرُ ثم يصير ترابا. الأمير والشنواني.
As for the miscarriage (1): if it is expelled after the blowing of the spirit into it, it is resurrected (2); otherwise it is like the rest of inanimate matter (3). (1) His statement: 'al-siqtu (miscarriage)' i.e., one for whom six months have not been completed. Al-Shanwani. (2) His statement: 'bu'itha (it is resurrected)' i.e., it is restored with its spirit, and when it enters Paradise it becomes like its inhabitants in beauty and height. Al-Shanwani. (3) His statement: 'al-mawāt (inanimate)' with two fatha's, lightened, like solid matter, which is a body that has no spirit, like a stone; it is gathered then becomes dust. Al-Amir and Al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a legal and theological ruling concerning a miscarriage (siqt). The author presents a conditional: if the fetus is expelled after the spirit has been blown into it (which occurs at 120 days according to hadith), then it will be resurrected on the Day of Resurrection. If it was expelled before the spirit entered it, it is treated like other inanimate matter (mawāt) — it will be gathered but then turned to dust, not given a spiritual existence. The footnotes clarify: 'siqt' refers to a fetus that has not completed six months; 'bu'itha' means it is restored with its spirit and in Paradise attains beauty and height like other inhabitants; 'mawāt' refers to a body without a spirit, like a stone, which is gathered then becomes dust. This shows that resurrection applies only to beings that had a spirit, and that the gathering of inanimate matter is only for the purpose of annihilation.

Definition of Resurrection and the Prophet's Precedence
Al-Bajuri defines ba‘th and nushūr and states the Prophet’s precedence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine of bodily resurrection (ba‘th and nushūr), the special precedence of the Prophet Muhammad, and the differing states of people on the Day of Gathering.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the physical re-creation of the body; the Prophet is the first to rise.

This lesson clarifies a key belief about the afterlife: that resurrection is a real, bodily event. The author first defines the terms ba‘th and nushūr as identical, then highlights the Prophet’s unique honor as the first to be resurrected, and finally explains that people’s states in the gathering reflect their deeds.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of resurrection

This emphasizes physical resurrection.
2

This is based on hadith.
3

Read the last part about people coming as riders, walkers, or on faces. Understand that this variety reflects their deeds.
This shows justice and individual accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والبعث والنشور عبارة عن معنى واحد، وهو: الإخراج من القبور بعد الأجزاء الأصليّة وإعادة الأرواح إليها كما علمت. وأول من تنشق عنه الأرض نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، فهو أول من يبعث، وأول وارد المحشر، كما أنه أول داخل الجنة، ومراتب الناس في الحشر متفاوتة لتفاوت مراتبهم في الأعمال؛ فمنهم الراكب، والماشي على رجليه أو وجهه.

And the first from whom the earth will split open is our Prophet Muḥammad (peace and blessings of Allāh be upon him); thus he is the first to be resurrected, and the first to arrive at the place of gathering (al-maḥshar), just as he is the first to enter Paradise. And the ranks of people in the gathering are varied according to the variation of their ranks in deeds; so among them are the rider, the one walking on his feet, and the one [walking] on his face.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage provides a doctrinal definition of the resurrection and highlights the special status of the Prophet Muḥammad in it. The author first equates the two terms ba‘th and nushūr, stating that they refer to the same reality: the removal of bodies from graves after the original components (the essential parts that define the person) have been gathered and souls are returned to them. This reaffirms the physical resurrection. Next, he mentions that the first to be resurrected is the Prophet Muḥammad; he is the first to have the earth split open for him, the first to rise, the first to arrive at the gathering place (al-maḥshar), and the first to enter Paradise. This is based on prophetic traditions. Finally, the author notes that people will come to the gathering in different states—some riding, some walking, some crawling on their faces—corresponding to their deeds in the world. This shows that the resurrection and gathering account for individual differences in faith and action.

The Four Types of Gathering (Hashr)
Al-Bajuri enumerates the four types of hashr (gathering): two in this world and two in the Hereafter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four types of hashr (gathering) as classified by Al-Bajuri, including the two worldly and two otherworldly gatherings.

Core Idea
Hashr has four stages: two before the Hour and two after.

Al-Bajuri presents a clear classification of the eschatological events known as hashr. He distinguishes between gatherings in this world and those in the afterlife. This passage helps us see the comprehensive nature of divine gathering across time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation to understand the basic meaning.
Notice the clear enumeration: 'four: two in this world... two in the Hereafter'.
2

Find the two types that occur in this world: the expulsion of the Jews and the driving of the fire before the Hour.
These are based on hadith reports.
3
Identify the two otherworldly gatherings
Find the two types that occur in the Hereafter: assembly at the standing-place and dispatch to Paradise or Hell.
These relate to the final judgment.
4
Reflect on the progression
Consider how the gatherings move from worldly events to the ultimate eternal destinies.
This shows the comprehensive plan of Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنواع الحشر أربعة: اثنان في الدنيا، أحدهما: إجلاؤه اليهود، وثانيهما: سوق النار الناس قرب قيام الساعة، واثنان في الآخرة، أحدهما جمعهم إلى الموقف بعد إحيائهم، والثاني: صرفهم من الموقف إلى الجنة أو النار.
And the types of gathering (al-ḥashr) are four: two in this world—one of them: the expulsion of the Jews [to Syria], and the second: the driving of the fire of the people near the establishment of the Hour—and two in the Hereafter—one of them: their assembly at the standing-place (al-mawqif) after their revivification, and the second: their dispatch from the standing-place to Paradise or Hell.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage classifies the eschatological events known as hashr (gathering). The author presents four distinct types, divided into two categories: those occurring in this world (al-dunyā) and those occurring in the Hereafter (al-ākhira). The first worldly type is the expulsion of the Jews from Arabia to Syria, based on prophetic traditions. The second is the driving of a great fire that will gather people before the Hour, as described in hadith literature. In the Hereafter, the first type is the assembly of all resurrected beings at the standing-place (al-mawqif) after they have been brought back to life. The second is the sending of people from the standing-place to their final abode: either Paradise or Hell. This enumeration highlights the comprehensive nature of divine gathering across different stages of the end of time, and emphasizes that the final judgment leads to eternal destinations.

The Two Views on Bodily Resurrection and Their Scope
Explanation of two views on bodily resurrection and their restriction to prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two theological opinions on how bodies are restored in the resurrection, and why this disagreement is limited to prophets and specific individuals.

Core Idea
Bodily resurrection is certain; the debate is over whether God recreates from nothing or from scattered parts.

The resurrection of bodies is a core belief in Islam, but theological schools differed on the precise mechanism. The author of the Jawharat al-Tawhid presents two views: restoration from pure non-existence or from pure dispersion. He then clarifies that this particular debate does not apply to all people, but only to prophets and those explicitly mentioned in revelation. This lesson unpacks these views and their scope.

Guided Path
1
Start with the passage context
Read the passage orientation and the translation to get the big picture of what the passage is about.
The passage discusses the return of bodies to the gathering place and two events in the afterlife.
2
Identify the two views
Find the two opinions: restoration from pure non-existence (al-'adam al-maḥḍ) and restoration from pure dispersion (al-tafrīq al-maḥḍ). Note which view the author presents decisively and which with doubt.
The first view is attributed to Ahl al-Ḥaqq and the Mu'tazila.
3
Understand the restriction
Notice that the author restricts this disagreement to the prophets and those upon whom it is explicitly stated. Understand why this distinction matters.
The disagreement is not general; for ordinary people, the resurrection is clear.
4
Explore the commentary
Read the commentary to see how each view is explained: the first view involves annihilation and recreation, the second involves removal of essence and trace. Also note the definition of 'body' in kalam.
The commentary clarifies that the restored body is the same as the first, not a similar one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عود الأجسام إلى المحشر (١)، واثنان في الآخرة، أحدهما جمعهم إلى الموقف بعد إحيائهم، والثاني: صرفهم من الموقف إلى الجنة أو النار.
وَقُلْ يُعَادُ الجِسْمُ بالتَّحْقِيقِ عَنْ عَدَمٍ وَقِيلَ عَن تفريقِ مَحْضَينِ لكنْ ذا الخلافُ خُصَّا بِالْأَنْبِيَا وَمَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ نُصَّـــا
ولما ذكر أن إعادة الأجسام حق يجب الإيمان بها .. ذكر الخلاف فيما عنه إعادتها: هل هو العدم المحض أو التفرق المحض؟ مشيرًا للأول بقوله: (وَقُلْ) أيها المكلف القائل ببعث الحشر ـ وهو المعاد الجسماني ـ قولا مطابقا لاعتقادك: إنه يُعادُ الجسم) أي: يعيده الله تعالى (بِالتَّحْقِيقِ) متعلق بـ«قل» أو بـ «يُعاد» إعادةً ناشئة عن عدم محض، فيعدم الله العالم بلا واسطة، فيصير معدوما بالكلية، كما أوجده كذلك فصار موجوداً، ثم يوجده، هذا قول أهل الحقِّ والمعتزلة القائلين بصحة الفناء على الأجسام، بل بوقوعه، وهو الصحيح، ولذا قدمه جازما به. وحكى مقابله بصيغة التمريض، أعنى قوله: (وَقِيلَ) تعاد الأجسام للحشر إعادة ناشئة (عَنْ تَفْرِيقِ مَحْضَيْنِ) فيذهب الله تعالى العين والأثر جميعاً، بحيث لا يبقى في الجسم جوهران فردان على الاتصال. والجسم عند المتكلمين: هو الجوهر القابل للانقسام، أو ما قام بذاته من العالم.
وأشار بقوله (بالتحقيق) إلى أن الجسم الثاني المعاد هو الأول المعدوم بعينه لا مثله.
ولما لم يكن هذا الخلاف على إطلاقه أشار إلى تقييده بقوله: (لَكِنْ ذَا الخلافُ خُصَّا بِالْأَنْبِيَا وَمَنْ عَلَيْهِمْ نُصَّا).
The return of bodies to the place of gathering, and two [things] in the afterlife: one is gathering them to the station after their revival, and the second is sending them from the station to Paradise or Hell. And say: the body is truly restored from non-existence, and it was said from two pure dispersions, but this difference is restricted to the prophets and those upon whom it is explicitly stated. And when he mentioned that the restoration of bodies is true and must be believed, he mentioned the disagreement concerning what they are restored from: is it pure non-existence or pure dispersion? Pointing to the first with his saying: (And say) O responsible one who affirms the resurrection of the gathering—which is the bodily return—a statement conforming to your belief: that the body is restored, meaning God restores it, with (truly) being attached to 'say' or to 'is restored,' a restoration arising from pure non-existence. So God annihilates the world without intermediary, and it becomes entirely non-existent, just as He brought it into existence similarly, so it became existent; then He creates it. This is the statement of the people of truth and the Mu'tazila who affirm the validity of annihilation of bodies, rather its occurrence, and it is correct; therefore he presented it decisively. And he narrated its opposite in the form of expressing doubt, namely his saying: (and it was said) the bodies are restored for the gathering a restoration arising from two pure dispersions; so God removes the essence and the trace entirely, such that no two individual atoms remain in the body in contact. And the body according to the mutakallimūn is the substance capable of division, or that which subsists by itself from the world. And he indicated by his saying (truly) that the second body restored is the first non-existent one itself, not its like. And since this disagreement was not absolute, he pointed to its restriction by his saying: (but this difference is restricted to the prophets and those upon whom it is explicitly stated).
Source pages p. 512

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a verse from the Jawharat al-Tawhid concerning the resurrection of bodies. It begins by setting the context: the return of bodies to the gathering place (al-maḥshar) and two events in the afterlife: gathering to the standing after revival, and then sending them to Paradise or Hell. The verse then states the two views: the body is truly restored from non-existence, and it was said from two pure dispersions, but this disagreement is restricted to the prophets and those explicitly mentioned. The commentary explains that the author of the poem first affirms that bodily resurrection is a truth that must be believed. Then he discusses the disagreement on what they are restored from: is it pure non-existence (al-'adam al-maḥḍ) or pure dispersion (al-tafrīq al-maḥḍ)? He points to the first view with the word 'qul' (say): the responsible believer should state that the body is restored from pure non-existence, meaning God annihilates the world without intermediary, then recreates it. This is the view of Ahl al-Ḥaqq and the Mu'tazila who affirm the possibility and occurrence of annihilation (fanā') of bodies. The commentator notes that this is the correct view and therefore the author presented it decisively. The opposite view is introduced with the expression of doubt ('qīla'): the body is restored from two pure dispersions, meaning God removes both the essence and the trace completely, leaving no two individual atoms in contact. The commentator then defines 'body' in kalam terminology: it is the substance (jawhar) capable of division, or what subsists by itself from the world. Next, the commentator explains that the word 'bi-l-taḥqīq' (truly) indicates that the second body restored is the very same as the first non-existent body, not a similar one. Finally, he notes that this disagreement is not absolute; it is restricted to the prophets and those specifically mentioned in revelation, meaning that for ordinary people, the resurrection is clear and not subject to this debate.

التفريق المحض

المعاد الجسماني
أهل الحق
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the Mu'tazila and Ahl al-Sunna disagree on all resurrection details, but here they agree on the possibility of annihilation.
Correction: The passage shows that both groups affirm bodily resurrection, and the disagreement is only about the mode (from non-existence vs. dispersion) and is restricted to prophets.

Checkpoint

A) Whether bodies are restored from pure non-existence or from pure dispersion
B) Whether prophets are resurrected or not
C) Whether the body is the same as the soul
D) Whether the resurrection occurs in this world or the next

Key Takeaway
The debate on how bodies are restored is a nuanced theological issue, but the certainty of bodily resurrection is agreed upon, and the disagreement is limited to prophets.

?

?

The Resurrection of Bodies and the Exception for Prophets
Al-Shanwani explains the correct view on bodily resurrection and the exception for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct Sunni view on bodily resurrection, the identity of the resurrected body, and the scriptural exceptions to the general principle.

Core Idea
Bodies are annihilated and recreated, not merely reassembled, with exceptions revealed by scripture.

Al-Shanwani begins by stating the correct view of Ahl al-Haqq and the Mu'tazila: bodies become non-existent and are then recreated by Allah. He also presents an opposing view that bodies are restored from complete dissolution, then clarifies that the resurrected body is numerically identical to the original. However, this disagreement is not universal—prophets and certain others are exempt because their bodies are preserved from decay. The passage concludes that this matter is tawqifiyya, relying solely on revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Notice the key terms and structure.
The passage is from the section on Sam'iyyat (scriptural matters).
2
Identify the two views on resurrection
The passage contrasts the correct view (annihilation and recreation) with an opposing view (restoration from two pure dissolutions). Note how the author signals certainty for the first and hedging for the second.
The hedging phrase is 'qila' (it is said).
3
Understand the identity of the resurrected body
The author emphasizes that the restored body is numerically identical to the first, not a mere likeness. This is indicated by 'bi-l-tahqiq' (with verification).
This counters the misconception of a 'different copy'.
4
Recognize the restriction of the disagreement
Al-Shanwani states that the disagreement about annihilation does not apply to prophets and certain others, as their bodies are not consumed by the earth. Note the list of exceptions.
The list includes prophets, martyrs, muezzins, bearers of Qur'an, sinless, scholars, spirit, tailbone, Paradise, Hell, Throne, etc.
5
Reflect on the principle of tawqifiyya
The passage ends by stating that this matter is tawqifiyya—dependent on revealed texts, not rational deduction. Why is this important?
This means these exceptions are known only through scripture.

Source Text

قسم السمعيات
موجوداً ، ثُمَّ يوجده ، هذا قول أهل الحقِّ والمعتزلة القائلين بصحة الفناء على الأجسام، بل بوقوعه ، وهو الصحيح ، ولذا قدَّمه جازما به .
وحَكَى مُقابله بصيغة التّمريض، أعنى قوله : (وَقِيلَ) تُعاد الأجسامُ للحشر إعادةٌ نَاشِئَةٌ (عَنْ تَفْرِيقِ مَحْضَيْنِ) فيُذْهِبُ الله تعالى العين والأثر جميعاً ، بحيث لا يبقى في الجسم جوهران فردان على الاتصال. والجسم عند المُتكلّمين : هو الجوهر القابل للانقسام، أو ما قام بذاته من العالم.

Section on Sam'iyyat (scriptural matters). It [the body] exists, then He creates it [again]. This is the statement of the People of Truth (Ahl al-Haqq) and the Mu'tazila who affirm the validity of annihilation (fana') of bodies, nay, its occurrence, and it is the correct [view], and therefore he [the author] presented it with certainty. And he mentioned its opposite in the style of hedging, i.e., his statement: 'And it is said: The bodies are restored for the Gathering (al-Hashr) a restoration arising from two pure dissolutions (tafriq mahdayn), and Allah makes the essence and the trace disappear entirely, such that there does not remain in the body two individual atoms (jawharan fardan) in contact.' And the body according to the theologians (al-mutakallimun) is the substance (jawhar) divisible, or what subsists by itself from the world. And he indicated by his statement (bi-l-tahqiq) that the second body restored is the first non-existent body itself, not its likeness. And since this disagreement was not unrestricted, he indicated its restriction by his statement: 'But this disagreement is specified (khussa)' i.e., some scholars restricted its generality to the prophets (bi-l-anbiya'), for the earth does not consume their bodies, nor does it wear out their frames by agreement. 'And those over them (wa man 'alayhim)' i.e., it was also specified for those persons (ashkhas) regarding whom the Lawgiver (al-shari') explicitly stated that the earth does not consume their bodies: such as the martyrs (shuhada'), the muezzins who give the call [seeking reward], the bearer of the Qur'an (hamil al-Qur'an), the one who has not committed sin, the knowledgeable scholars, the spirit (al-ruh), the tailbone (ajb al-dhanab), Paradise (al-janna) and Hellfire (al-nar) and their inhabitants, the Throne (al-'arsh) and the Chair (al-kursi), the Tablet (al-lawh) and the Pen (al-qalam). And the matter is tawqifiyya (dependent on revealed texts).
Source pages p. 513

Commentary
This passage defines the correct position regarding the resurrection of bodies, addresses a contrary view, clarifies the identity of the resurrected body, and then qualifies the disagreement with an exception based on revealed texts. The passage is part of the section on sam'iyyat (matters known from scripture). The author begins by stating the correct view: that bodies become non-existent and then are recreated by God. This is the view of Ahl al-Haqq and the Mu'tazila, who hold that annihilation (fana') is possible for bodies and actually occurs. Then he mentions the opposing view (introduced with 'qila', a hedging formula) that bodies are restored from a state of 'two pure dissolutions', meaning that the body is completely disintegrated so that no two individual atoms remain in contact. The author then defines the body for the theologians: it is a substance (jawhar) that is divisible, or what subsists by itself. Next, he clarifies that the second body is numerically identical to the first, not a mere likeness, indicated by the phrase 'bi-l-tahqiq' (with verification). Then he restricts the scope of this disagreement: it does not apply to prophets and certain specified individuals, because their bodies are not consumed by the earth. He lists these exceptions: prophets, martyrs, muezzins calling to prayer seeking reward, the bearer of the Qur'an, the sinless, knowledgeable scholars, the spirit (al-ruh), the tailbone (ajb al-dhanab), Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants, the Throne, the Chair, the Tablet, and the Pen. The passage concludes that this matter is tawqifiyya, meaning it rests solely on revealed texts rather than reason.
