Obligation of Believing in the Taking of Records
The author explains the obligation of believing in the taking of records on the Day of Judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that believing in the taking of records on the Day of Judgment is obligatory based on revelation, and that it includes all morally responsible beings.

Core Idea
Belief in the taking of records is wajib because it is proven by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

In this passage, the author establishes that the taking of records is a real event of the Day of Judgment that we must believe in. He clarifies that the obligation comes from revealed sources and that it applies to all accountable beings. The commentary explains the reasoning behind this ruling, including the mention of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning, who are still included in the general taking of records but exempt from the full reckoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the author's style: he begins by describing the taking of records with joy, then quotes his teacher, then presents the poetic line and its commentary.
Pay attention to the phrase 'وَوَاجِبٌ سَمْعًا' which indicates the basis of obligation.
2
Identify the evidence for obligation
The commentary states that the obligation is based on revelation (sam'an) because it is conveyed in the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. Also note the principle: everything that is possible and proven by definitive evidence is real and must be believed.
3
Understand the scope of the obligation
The 'taking' applies to the category of the servants (jins al-ibad) from the morally responsible among humans and jinn. This includes even the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning, but they are exempt from the accounting itself.
The exception does not negate the general obligation to believe in the taking of records for all.
4
Reflect on the signs of the Hour
The passage also mentions belief in the widely transmitted signs of the Hour, which are accepted in general, but the exact time is known only to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخذُ العباد صُحُفَ أعمالهم يومَ القيامة من السرور والنّضْرَة والحَبُور ، قال أستاذنا رحمه الله تعالى: وهذا هو الَّذي أعتقده، لكني لم أقف عليه مُصرَّحاً به في كلامهم. وكذا الإيمان أيضا بما تواتر من علاماته الدالة على ثبوته إجمالاً ؛ لأنَّه لا يعلم عينه إلا الله .
١٠٤. وواجبٌ أَخُذُ العِبَادِ الصُّحُفَا كَمَا مِنَ القُرآن نَصَّا عُرِفَا
ثمَّ شرعَ في الكلام على شيء من الأهوال فقال: (وَوَاجِبٌ) سمعاً ؛ لِوُرودِهِ كِتابًا وسُنَّةً وانعقادِ الإجماع عليه ، مع إمكانه ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك فهو واقع ، والإيمان به واجبٌ (أَخْذُ ) ، أي : تناولُ جِنس (العِبَادِ) مِن مُكلَّفي الثقلين ، فلا يَرِدُ السَّبعونَ ألفًا الذين يدخلون الجنَّة بغير حساب.
The taking of the records of deeds by the servants on the Day of Resurrection includes joy, radiance, and delight. Our teacher, may Allah have mercy on him, said: This is what I believe, but I have not found it explicitly stated in their words. Likewise, belief is also required in what has been widely transmitted of its signs that indicate its occurrence in general, because no one knows its exact time except Allah.
104. And it is obligatory that the servants take the records, as known from the text of the Quran.
Then he began to speak about some of the terrors and said: (And it is obligatory) by revelation, because it is conveyed in the Book and the Sunnah, and consensus has been established upon it, along with its possibility. And everything that is so is real, and belief in it is obligatory: (taking) i.e., the taking of the category of the servants from the morally responsible among the two heavy burdens (jinn and humans). So the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning are not excepted.
Source pages p. 531

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation of believing in the taking of the records of deeds on the Day of Judgment. The author begins by mentioning that the taking of records includes joy, radiance, and delight. He then quotes his teacher stating a personal belief that this is so, though he has not found it explicitly stated in previous scholars' words. This indicates that while the general reality of the taking of records is established by revelation, the specific details of the believers' joy upon receiving their records in the right hand are derived from scriptural inference. Next, the author asserts that belief is also required in the widely transmitted signs of the Hour, which indicate its occurrence in general, without specifying the exact time, which only Allah knows.

Then the author presents the poetic line (number 104 of the poem): 'And it is obligatory that the servants take the records, as known from the text of the Quran.' This line encapsulates the ruling: taking the records is wajib (obligatory) to believe in because it is proven by the Quran.

The commentary that follows explains the line: the obligation is based on revelation (sam'an) – because the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus confirm it, along with its logical possibility. The author states that anything that is proven by definitive evidence and is possible must be real. Therefore, believing in it is wajib. The term 'taking' refers to the action of the category of the servants, specifically those who are morally responsible (mukallafun) from among humans and jinn. The exception of the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning does not contradict this general obligation, as they are included in the 'category' but are saved from the terrors of the judgment.

اليوم الآخر

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the taking of records only applies to sinful people or that the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning do not have their records taken at all.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the taking of records applies to all morally responsible beings, including the seventy thousand. However, the latter are exempt from the accounting but still receive their records.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the obligation to believe in the taking of records?
A) Logical necessity alone
B) The Quran, Sunnah, and consensus
C) The opinion of the author's teacher
D) The consensus of the seventy thousand

Key Takeaway
Belief in the taking of records is obligatory for every morally responsible being, as it is established by Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, and it is a real event of the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The author says that belief in the taking of records is obligatory. Is your belief in this reality strong enough to affect how you speak, act, and think? In what specific area of your life is your belief weakest, and what step will you take this week to strengthen it?
?
The seventy thousand who enter Paradise without reckoning are not exempt from taking their records. Do you strive to be among those who receive their records with joy and radiance? What deed can you do today to increase your hope of being among them?

The Obligation of Receiving the Books of Deeds
Sanusi rules on the obligation of taking the books and gives evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why believing in the taking of the books on the Day of Judgment is obligatory and how it is established by revelation and reason.

Core Idea
The taking of the books is a real event, obligatory to believe, confirmed by scripture and reason.

In this lesson, we examine Sanusi's ruling on an eschatological event: the servants receiving their books of deeds. The passage not only declares belief in this event obligatory but also provides a concise proof based on revelation, consensus, and rational possibility. Understanding this helps solidify the foundation of the sam'iyyat (matters heard through revelation) in Islamic creed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic line from the matn and the commentator's expansion carefully. Then read the literal English translation. Let the text speak before you analyze.
Notice the concise style: the matn gives the ruling, and the commentary unpacks the evidence.
2
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage states that 'taking of the books' is wajib (obligatory) to believe. See how the commentator justifies this with three sources: Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma' (consensus).
The phrase 'sam'an' indicates the obligation is derived from revelation.
3
Understand the principle of possibility and reality
The commentator adds that the event is rationally possible, and whatever is possible and confirmed by revelation is real (waqi'). Therefore, belief is obligatory. This links reason and revelation.
4
Grasp the clarification about the seventy thousand
The passage specifies that 'the servants' refers to all obligated beings (humans and jinn) except those who enter Paradise without account. This guards against misunderstanding that everyone receives a book.
The seventy thousand are an exception by divine mercy, not a contradiction to the general rule.
5
Reflect on the takeaway
Summarize: belief in the taking of the books is obligatory because it is established by Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', and is possible. This is a core element of faith in the unseen.
This lesson reinforces the methodology of affirming eschatological events when they are textually and rationally sound.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٠٤. وَوَاجِبٌ أَخْذُ الْعِبَادِ الصُّحُفَا كَمَا مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ نَصًّا عُرِفَا. ثُمَّ شَرَعَ فِي الْكَلَامِ عَلَى شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْأَهْوَالِ فَقَالَ: (وَوَاجِبٌ) سَمْعًا؛ لِوُرُودِهِ كِتَابًا وَسُنَّةً وَانْعِقَادِ الْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَيْهِ، مَعَ إِمْكَانِهِ، وَكُلُّ مَا هُوَ كَذَلِكَ فَهُوَ وَاقِعٌ، وَالْإِيمَانُ بِهِ وَاجِبٌ (أَخْذُ) أَيْ: تَنَاوُلُ جِنْسِ (الْعِبَادِ) مِنْ مُكَلَّفِي الثَّقَلَيْنِ، فَلَا يَرِدُ السَّبْعُونَ أَلْفًا الَّذِينَ يَدْخُلُونَ الْجَنَّةَ بِغَيْرِ حِسَابٍ.
104. And obligatory is the taking of the servants of the books, as from the Quran by text it is known. Then he began to speak about some of the terrors and said: 'And it is obligatory' by revelation, due to its occurrence in the Book and the Sunnah and the consensus upon it, along with its possibility, and everything that is thus is real, and belief in it is obligatory. 'The taking' i.e., the receiving of the genus of 'the servants' from the obligated ones of the two heavy burdens, so the seventy thousand who enter Paradise without account are not included.
Source pages p. 532

Commentary
This passage is a theological ruling (hukm) regarding the eschatological event of the servants receiving their books of deeds on the Day of Judgment. It begins with the poetic line from the matn, which declares it obligatory to believe in the taking of the books, asserting that this is textually known from the Quran. The commentator then explains that the obligation is 'sam'an' (by revelation) because the event is established by the Quran, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the scholars. Additionally, it is rationally possible, and the principle is: whatever is possible and confirmed by revelation must be real (waqi'). Therefore, belief in it is wajib. The commentator further clarifies that 'the servants' (al-‘ibad) refers to the genus of obligated beings from the two heavy burdens (humans and jinn), thereby excluding the seventy thousand who will enter Paradise without any account. This clarification guards against the misunderstanding that everyone, including those saved by sheer mercy, must undergo the giving of books.

Key Terms
سمعيات
صحف
عباد
مكلفون
السبعون ألفًا

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that believing in the taking of the books is optional or not necessary.
Correction: The passage clearly states that it is wajib (obligatory) and real, supported by revelation, consensus, and rational possibility. Denying it would be a failure in required belief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the obligation to believe in the taking of the books?
A) Rational proof alone
B) The Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'
C) Consensus of the Sufis
D) Personal opinion

Key Takeaway
Belief in the receiving of the books on the Day of Judgment is obligatory and established by revelation, reason, and consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you knew that every deed you have done today is already recorded and will be handed to you on a day you cannot avoid, how would that change the way you act in the next hour? What is one specific action you will change today because of this certainty?
?
The passage says belief in the taking of books is obligatory. But do you truly live as if your deeds are being recorded? Or is there a gap between your mental assent and your daily conduct? What is one specific area where your actions do not match this belief, and what will you do tonight to bridge that gap?
?
The seventy thousand are exempt from this accounting—but you are not among them (unless Allah wills). How does that reality make you feel? Does it drive you to gratitude for Allah's mercy and urgency in your own preparation? Write down one concrete way you will prepare for that moment before you sleep tonight.

The Books of Deeds: Their Nature and Delivery Reconciled
The author explains the nature of the books and reconciles narrations about their delivery.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the books of deeds and how the apparent contradictions in the hadith about their delivery are reconciled.

Core Idea
The books of deeds are delivered by wind to the neck, then angels place them in the hands.

This passage from the Sam'iyyat section addresses the eschatological reality of the books of deeds. The author clarifies what these books are, how the daily records are compiled, and reconciles the two apparently different narrations about how each person receives their book. Understanding this reconciliation is important for a consistent belief in the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Pay attention to the flow from definition to reconciliation.
2
Identify the definition and two opinions on compilation
Note the definition of 'suhuf' as the books of deeds written by angels. Then find the two opinions: some say daily records are joined, others say all are copied into one book.
The author mentions both without preference.
3
Examine the two narrations on delivery
Notice the wind narration (wind flies books from beneath the Throne to the neck) and the calling narration (each person is called and given his book).
These seem contradictory at first.
4
Understand the reconciliation
The passage reconciles by saying angels take the books from the necks and place them in the hands, combining both narrations.
This preserves both hadith as complementary.
5
Reflect on the significance
Reflect on why this detail matters for eschatological belief: it shows the precision and care in narrating unseen events.
It also demonstrates how apparent contradictions in hadith can be harmonized.

قسم السمعيات. وَلَا الْمَلَائِكَةُ وَلَا الْأَنْبِيَاءُ؛ فَإِنَّهُمْ لَا يَأْخُذُونَ الصُّحُفَا الْمُرَادُ مِنْهَا: الْكُتُبُ الَّتِي كَتَبَتِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ فِيهَا مَا فَعَلُوهُ فِي الدُّنْيَا، وَعَلَى هَذَا فَقِيلَ: تُوصَلُ صُحُفُ الْأَيَّامِ وَاللَّيَالِي، وَقِيلَ: يُنْسَخُ مَا فِي جَمِيعِهَا فِي صَحِيفَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ، وَجُمِعَ الصُّحُفُ لِمُقَابَلَةِ الْعِبَادِ، وَلَمْ يَذْكُرِ الْمُصَنِّفُ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى دَافِعَ جَمْعِ الصُّحُفِ؛ لِمَا وَرَدَ أَنَّ الرِّيحَ تُطِيرُهَا مِنْ خِزَانَةٍ تَحْتَ الْعَرْشِ فَلَا تُخْطِئُ صَحِيفَةٌ عُنُقَ صَاحِبِهَا، وَأَنَّ كُلَّ أَحَدٍ يُدْعَى فَيُعْطَى كِتَابَهُ، وَجُمِعَ: بِأَنَّ الْمَلَائِكَةَ تَأْخُذُهَا مِنَ الْأَعْنَاقِ وَتَضَعُهَا فِي الْأَيْدِي.
Section of the Sam'iyyat. And not the angels nor the prophets, for they do not take the books. The intended meaning (of the books) is: the books in which the angels wrote what they did in the world. And on this it is said: the books of the days and nights are joined together. And it is said: what is in all of them is copied into one book. And the plural 'books' is used for the sake of correspondence with the servants. And the author (may Allah have mercy on him) did not mention the impeller of the collection of the books because of what was narrated: that the wind flies them from a repository beneath the Throne, and no book misses the neck of its owner, and that every person is called and is given his book. And it is reconciled: that the angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands.
Source pages p. 533

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the nature and delivery of the books (suhuf) of deeds. It begins by specifying that angels and prophets are not included among those who receive these books, likely because they are not from the obligated ones in the same sense as humans and jinn. The books are defined as the records written by angels of each person's deeds in the world. The text then addresses the apparent multiplicity of books: some say the daily and nightly records are joined together into one, while others say all are compiled into a single book. The plural 'suhuf' is used because of the plurality of servants. The author did not specify the agent that delivers the books, and the reason given is that there are two types of narrations: one that the wind flies the books from a repository beneath the Throne and they attach to the necks of their owners, and another that each person is called and given his book directly. These are reconciled by stating that the wind brings them to the necks, and then the angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands of the owners. This preserves both sets of hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the hadith about the wind and the hadith about being called are contradictory.
Correction: This passage shows that they are complementary: the wind brings the books to the neck, then angels take them and place them in the hands.

Checkpoint
How does the author reconcile the narration that the wind brings the books to the necks with the narration that each person is called and given his book?
A) One narration is rejected as weak
B) The wind is a metaphor for angels
C) The angels take them from the necks and place them in the hands
D) The books are given to the prophets first

Key Takeaway
The books of deeds are initially attached to the neck by wind, then angels place them in the hands of each person.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You will receive a book that contains every deed you have done. What did you do today that you would be ashamed to see written there? Will you repent and change that action before it is recorded?
?
The wind delivers the book to your neck, and an angel places it in your hand. Imagine holding that book. What would you want the first page to say about your intentions and actions?
?
If you knew that every word you speak tonight will be written and presented to you on that day, what would you say differently before you sleep?
